development.<sup id="cite_ref-cientifico_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cientifico-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Various iconic buildings and monuments were initiated by D\xc3\xadaz, including the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Correos_de_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Palacio de Correos de Mexico">Palacio de Correos de Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monumento_a_la_Independencia" class="mw-redirect" title="Monumento a la Independencia">Monumento a la Independencia</a> and the Palacio Legislativo (which became the <a href="/wiki/Monumento_a_la_Revoluci%C3%B3n" title="Monumento a la Revoluci\xc3\xb3n">Monumento a la Revoluci\xc3\xb3n</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Mexican_Revolution_.281910.E2.80.931920.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexican_Revolution_(1910\xe2\x80\x931920)">Mexican Revolution (1910\xe2\x80\x931920)</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg/220px-Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg/330px-Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e5/Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg 2x" data-file-width="425" data-file-height="297" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Madero_en_Cuernavaca.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Francisco_I._Madero" title="Francisco I. Madero">Francisco I. Madero</a> with <a href="/wiki/Emiliano_Zapata" title="Emiliano Zapata">Emiliano Zapata</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a></div></div></div>\n<p>President D\xc3\xadaz announced in 1908 that he would retire in 1911, resulting in the development of new coalitions. But then he ran for reelection anyway and in a show of U.S. support, D\xc3\xadaz and <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a> planned a summit in El Paso, Texas, and Ciudad Ju\xc3\xa1rez, Mexico, for October 16, 1909, an historic first meeting between a Mexican and a U.S. president and also the first time an American president would cross the border into Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris2009_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris2009-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Both sides agreed that the disputed <a href="/wiki/Chamizal_dispute" title="Chamizal dispute">Chamizal strip</a> connecting El Paso to Ciudad Ju\xc3\xa1rez would be considered neutral territory with no flags present during the summit, but the meeting focused attention on this territory and resulted in assassination threats and other serious security concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris2009_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris2009-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the day of the summit, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Russell_Burnham" title="Frederick Russell Burnham">Frederick Russell Burnham</a>, the celebrated scout, and Private C.R. Moore, a <a href="/wiki/Texas_Ranger_Division" title="Texas Ranger Division">Texas Ranger</a>, discovered a man holding a concealed <a href="/wiki/Protector_Palm_Pistol" title="Protector Palm Pistol">palm pistol</a> standing at the El Paso Chamber of Commerce building along the procession route, and they disarmed the assassin within only a few feet of D\xc3\xadaz and Taft.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris2009_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris2009-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Both presidents were unharmed and the summit was held.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris2009_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris2009-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> D\xc3\xadaz was re-elected in 1910, but alleged electoral fraud forced him into exile in France and sparked the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">1910 Mexican Revolution</a>, initially led by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_I._Madero" title="Francisco I. Madero">Francisco I. Madero</a>.\n</p><p>Madero was elected president but <a href="/wiki/Decena_tr%C3%A1gica" class="mw-redirect" title="Decena tr\xc3\xa1gica">overthrown and murdered</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat">coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat</a> two years later directed by conservative general <a href="/wiki/Victoriano_Huerta" title="Victoriano Huerta">Victoriano Huerta</a>. That event re-ignited the civil war, involving figures such as <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Villa" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Villa">Francisco Villa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emiliano_Zapata" title="Emiliano Zapata">Emiliano Zapata</a>, who formed their own forces. A third force, the <a href="/wiki/Ej%C3%A9rcito_Constitucionalista" class="mw-redirect" title="Ej\xc3\xa9rcito Constitucionalista">constitutional army</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Venustiano_Carranza" title="Venustiano Carranza">Venustiano Carranza</a> managed to bring an end to the war, and radically amended the 1857 Constitution to include many of the social premises and demands of the revolutionaries into what was eventually called the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico" title="Constitution of Mexico">1917 Constitution</a>. It is estimated that the war killed 900,000 of the 1910 population of 15 million.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Assassinated in 1920, Carranza was succeeded by another revolutionary hero, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Obreg%C3%B3n" title="\xc3\x81lvaro Obreg\xc3\xb3n">\xc3\x81lvaro Obreg\xc3\xb3n</a>, who in turn was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Plutarco_El%C3%ADas_Calles" title="Plutarco El\xc3\xadas Calles">Plutarco El\xc3\xadas Calles</a>. Obreg\xc3\xb3n was reelected in 1928 but was assassinated before he could assume power. Although this period is usually referred to as the Mexican Revolution, it might also be termed a civil war since president D\xc3\xadaz (1909) narrowly escaped assassination and presidents Francisco I. Madero (1913), Venustiano Carranza (1920), \xc3\x81lvaro Obreg\xc3\xb3n (1928), and former revolutionary leaders Emiliano Zapata (1919) and Pancho Villa (1923) all were assassinated during this period.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Early-20th-century_stability_and_one-party_rule_.281920.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early-20th-century_stability_and_one-party_rule_(1920\xe2\x80\x932000)">Early-20th-century stability and one-party rule (1920\xe2\x80\x932000)</span></h3>\n<p>In 1929, Calles founded the National Revolutionary Party (PNR), later renamed the <a href="/wiki/Institutional_Revolutionary_Party" title="Institutional Revolutionary Party">Institutional Revolutionary Party</a> (PRI), and started a period known as the <a href="/wiki/Maximato" title="Maximato">Maximato</a>, which ended with the election of <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A1zaro_C%C3%A1rdenas" title="L\xc3\xa1zaro C\xc3\xa1rdenas">L\xc3\xa1zaro C\xc3\xa1rdenas</a>, who implemented many economic and social reforms. This included the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_oil_expropriation" title="Mexican oil expropriation">Mexican oil expropriation</a> in March 1938, which nationalized the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Anglo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> oil company known as the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Eagle_Petroleum_Company" title="Mexican Eagle Petroleum Company">Mexican Eagle Petroleum Company</a>. This movement would result in the creation of the state-owned Mexican oil company known as <a href="/wiki/Pemex" title="Pemex">Pemex</a>. This sparked a diplomatic crisis with the countries whose citizens had lost businesses by C\xc3\xa1rdenas\' radical measure, but since then the company has played an important role in the economic development of Mexico.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_(A68).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_%28A68%29.JPG/220px-Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_%28A68%29.JPG" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_%28A68%29.JPG/330px-Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_%28A68%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_%28A68%29.JPG/440px-Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_%28A68%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4512" data-file-height="2772" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estudiantes_sobre_cammi%C3%B3n_quemado_(A68).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Students in a burned bus during the <a href="/wiki/Tlatelolco_massacre" title="Tlatelolco massacre">protests of 1968</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1940 and 1980, Mexico remained a poor country but experienced substantial economic growth that some historians call the "<a href="/wiki/Mexican_miracle" title="Mexican miracle">Mexican miracle</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Although the economy continued to flourish for some, <a href="/wiki/Distribution_of_wealth" title="Distribution of wealth">social inequality</a> remained a factor of discontent. Moreover, the PRI rule became increasingly authoritarian and at times oppressive in what is now referred to as \'Mexico\'s dirty war\'<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> (see the <a href="/wiki/Tlatelolco_massacre" title="Tlatelolco massacre">1968 Tlatelolco massacre</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MMex_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MMex-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> which claimed the life of around 300 protesters based on conservative estimates and as many as 800 protesters).<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Electoral reforms and high oil prices followed the administration of <a href="/wiki/Luis_Echeverr%C3%ADa" title="Luis Echeverr\xc3\xada">Luis Echeverr\xc3\xada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crandall_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crandall-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> mismanagement of these revenues led to inflation and exacerbated the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_debt_crisis" title="Latin American debt crisis">1982 Crisis</a>. That year, <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">oil prices plunged</a>, interest rates soared, and the government defaulted on its <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">debt</a>. <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_la_Madrid" title="Miguel de la Madrid">President Miguel de la Madrid</a> resorted to currency devaluations which in turn sparked inflation.\n</p><p>In the 1980s the first cracks emerged in PRI\'s dominance. In <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Ruffo_Appel" title="Ernesto Ruffo Appel">Ernesto Ruffo Appel</a> was elected as governor. In 1988, alleged <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">electoral fraud</a> prevented the leftist candidate <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc_C%C3%A1rdenas" title="Cuauht\xc3\xa9moc C\xc3\xa1rdenas">Cuauht\xc3\xa9moc C\xc3\xa1rdenas</a> from winning the national presidential elections, giving <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Salinas_de_Gortari" title="Carlos Salinas de Gortari">Carlos Salinas de Gortari</a> the presidency and leading to massive protests in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nafta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nafta.jpg/220px-Nafta.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nafta.jpg/330px-Nafta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nafta.jpg/440px-Nafta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="715" data-file-height="481" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nafta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NAFTA signing ceremony, October 1992. From left to right: (standing) president <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Salinas_de_Gortari" title="Carlos Salinas de Gortari">Carlos Salinas de Gortari</a> (Mexico), president <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> (U.S.), and prime minister <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mulroney" title="Brian Mulroney">Brian Mulroney</a> (Canada); (seated) <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Serra_Puche" title="Jaime Serra Puche">Jaime Serra Puche</a> (Mexico), <a href="/wiki/Carla_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Carla Hills">Carla Hills</a> (U.S.), and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wilson_(Canadian_politician)" title="Michael Wilson (Canadian politician)">Michael Wilson</a> (Canada)</div></div></div>\n<p>Salinas embarked on a program of <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberal</a> reforms which fixed the exchange rate, controlled inflation, and culminated with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA), which came into effect on January 1, 1994. The same day, the <a href="/wiki/Zapatista_Army_of_National_Liberation" title="Zapatista Army of National Liberation">Zapatista Army of National Liberation</a> (EZLN) started a two-week-long armed rebellion against the federal government, and has continued as a non-violent opposition movement against <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>.\n</p><p>In 1994, Salinas was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Zedillo" title="Ernesto Zedillo">Ernesto Zedillo</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso_crisis" title="Mexican peso crisis">Mexican peso crisis</a> and a $50 billion <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> bailout. Major macroeconomic reforms were started by President Zedillo, and the economy rapidly recovered and growth peaked at almost 7% by the end of 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_Mexico">Contemporary Mexico</span></h3>\n<p>In 2000, after 71 years, the PRI lost a presidential election to <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Fox" title="Vicente Fox">Vicente Fox</a> of the opposition <a href="/wiki/National_Action_Party_(Mexico)" title="National Action Party (Mexico)">National Action Party</a> (PAN). In the 2006 presidential election, <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Felipe Calder\xc3\xb3n">Felipe Calder\xc3\xb3n</a> from the PAN was declared the winner, with a very narrow margin over leftist politician <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Manuel_L%C3%B3pez_Obrador" title="Andr\xc3\xa9s Manuel L\xc3\xb3pez Obrador">Andr\xc3\xa9s Manuel L\xc3\xb3pez Obrador</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_the_Democratic_Revolution" title="Party of the Democratic Revolution">Party of the Democratic Revolution</a> (PRD). L\xc3\xb3pez Obrador, however, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_general_election_2006_controversies" title="Mexican general election 2006 controversies">contested the election</a> and pledged to create an "alternative government".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After twelve years, in 2012, the PRI won the Presidency again with the election of <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Pe\xc3\xb1a Nieto">Enrique Pe\xc3\xb1a Nieto</a>, the governor of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a> from 2005\xe2\x80\x932011. However, he won with only a plurality of about 38%, and did not have a legislative majority.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In his third presidential run, former mayor of Mexico City Andr\xc3\xa9s Manuel L\xc3\xb3pez Obrador won the 2018 presidential election with over 50% of the vote. His political coalition, led by left-wing party <a href="/wiki/National_Regeneration_Movement" title="National Regeneration Movement">MORENA</a> which was founded after the 2012 elections by Andres himself, includes parties and politicians from all over the political spectrum and has also obtained the majority in both: upper and lower congress chambers. AMLO\'s (one his many nicknames) swept succes is attributed to the country\'s other strong political alternatives exhausting their chances as well as the politician adopting a moderate discourse with focus in conciliation.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mexico" title="Geography of Mexico">Geography of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Mexico_topo.jpg/300px-Mexico_topo.jpg" width="300" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Mexico_topo.jpg/450px-Mexico_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Mexico_topo.jpg/600px-Mexico_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="922" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Mexico</div></div></div>\n<p>Mexico is located between latitudes <a href="/wiki/14th_parallel_north" title="14th parallel north">14\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/33rd_parallel_north" title="33rd parallel north">33\xc2\xb0N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/86th_meridian_west" title="86th meridian west">86\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/119th_meridian_west" title="119th meridian west">119\xc2\xb0W</a> in the southern portion of North America. Almost all of Mexico lies in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American Plate</a>, with small parts of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">Pacific</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cocos_Plate" title="Cocos Plate">Cocos Plates</a>. <a href="/wiki/Geophysics" title="Geophysics">Geophysically</a>, some geographers include the territory east of the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Tehuantepec" title="Isthmus of Tehuantepec">Isthmus of Tehuantepec</a> (around 12% of the total) within Central America.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">Geopolitically</a>, however, Mexico is entirely considered part of North America, along with Canada and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico\'s total area is 1,972,550&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (761,606&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">world\'s 14th largest country by total area</a>. It has coastlines on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, the latter two forming part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Within these seas are about 6,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,317&#160;sq&#160;mi) of islands (including the remote Pacific <a href="/wiki/Guadalupe_Island" title="Guadalupe Island">Guadalupe Island</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Revillagigedo_Islands" title="Revillagigedo Islands">Revillagigedo Islands</a>). From its farthest land points, Mexico is a little over 2,000&#160;mi (3,219&#160;km) in length.\n</p><p>On its north, Mexico shares a 3,141&#160;km (1,952&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Mexico\xe2\x80\x93United States border">border with the United States</a>. The meandering <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Bravo_del_Norte" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Bravo del Norte">R\xc3\xado Bravo del Norte</a> (known as the Rio Grande in the United States) defines the border from <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Ciudad Ju\xc3\xa1rez">Ciudad Ju\xc3\xa1rez</a> east to the Gulf of Mexico. A series of natural and artificial markers delineate the United States-Mexican border west from Ciudad Ju\xc3\xa1rez to the Pacific Ocean. <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> made the construction of a border wall (on the U.S. side) an element of his 2016 presidential campaign. On its south, Mexico shares an 871&#160;km (541&#160;mi) border with Guatemala and a 251&#160;km (156&#160;mi) border with Belize.\n</p><p>Mexico is crossed from north to south by two mountain ranges known as <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_Oriental" title="Sierra Madre Oriental">Sierra Madre Oriental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_Occidental" title="Sierra Madre Occidental">Sierra Madre Occidental</a>, which are the extension of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> from northern North America. From east to west at the center, the country is crossed by the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Mexican_Volcanic_Belt" title="Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt">Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt</a> also known as the Sierra Nevada. A fourth mountain range, the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_del_Sur" title="Sierra Madre del Sur">Sierra Madre del Sur</a>, runs from <a href="/wiki/Michoac%C3%A1n" title="Michoac\xc3\xa1n">Michoac\xc3\xa1n</a> to <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nationsencyclopedia1_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationsencyclopedia1-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As such, the majority of the Mexican central and northern territories are located at high altitudes, and the highest elevations are found at the Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt: <a href="/wiki/Pico_de_Orizaba" title="Pico de Orizaba">Pico de Orizaba</a> (5,700&#160;m or 18,701&#160;ft), <a href="/wiki/Popocat%C3%A9petl" title="Popocat\xc3\xa9petl">Popocat\xc3\xa9petl</a> (5,462&#160;m or 17,920&#160;ft) and <a href="/wiki/Iztaccihuatl" title="Iztaccihuatl">Iztaccihuatl</a> (5,286&#160;m or 17,343&#160;ft) and the <a href="/wiki/Nevado_de_Toluca" title="Nevado de Toluca">Nevado de Toluca</a> (4,577&#160;m or 15,016&#160;ft). Three major urban agglomerations are located in the valleys between these four elevations: <a href="/wiki/Toluca" title="Toluca">Toluca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Mexico_City" title="Greater Mexico City">Greater Mexico City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puebla,_Puebla" class="mw-redirect" title="Puebla, Puebla">Puebla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nationsencyclopedia1_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationsencyclopedia1-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Mexico" title="Climate of Mexico">Climate of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/300px-Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" width="300" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/450px-Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/600px-Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="765" data-file-height="765" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mexico map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a> effectively divides the country into temperate and tropical zones. Land north of the twenty-fourth parallel experiences cooler temperatures during the winter months. South of the twenty-fourth parallel, temperatures are fairly constant year round and vary solely as a function of elevation. This gives Mexico one of the world\'s most diverse weather systems.\n</p><p>Areas south of the 24th parallel with elevations up to 1,000&#160;m (3,281&#160;ft) (the southern parts of both coastal plains as well as the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucat\xc3\xa1n Peninsula">Yucat\xc3\xa1n Peninsula</a>), have a yearly median temperature between 24 to 28&#160;\xc2\xb0C (75.2 to 82.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Temperatures here remain high throughout the year, with only a 5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (9&#160;\xc2\xb0F) difference between winter and summer median temperatures. Both Mexican coasts, except for the south coast of the Bay of Campeche and northern Baja, are also vulnerable to serious <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">hurricanes</a> during the summer and fall. Although low-lying areas north of the 24th parallel are hot and humid during the summer, they generally have lower yearly temperature averages (from 20 to 24&#160;\xc2\xb0C or 68.0 to 75.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) because of more moderate conditions during the winter.\n</p><p>Many large cities in Mexico are located in the Valley of Mexico or in adjacent valleys with altitudes generally above 2,000&#160;m (6,562&#160;ft). This gives them a year-round temperate climate with yearly temperature averages (from 16 to 18&#160;\xc2\xb0C or 60.8 to 64.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and cool nighttime temperatures throughout the year.\n</p><p>Many parts of Mexico, particularly the north, have a dry climate with sporadic rainfall while parts of the tropical lowlands in the south average more than 2,000&#160;mm (78.7&#160;in) of annual precipitation. For example, many cities in the north like <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hermosillo" title="Hermosillo">Hermosillo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mexicali" title="Mexicali">Mexicali</a> experience temperatures of 40&#160;\xc2\xb0C (104&#160;\xc2\xb0F) or more in summer. In the <a href="/wiki/Sonoran_Desert" title="Sonoran Desert">Sonoran Desert</a> temperatures reach 50&#160;\xc2\xb0C (122&#160;\xc2\xb0F) or more.\n</p><p>In 2012, Mexico passed a comprehensive climate change bill, a first in the developing world, that has set a goal for the country to generate 35% of its energy from clean energy sources by 2024, and to cut emissions by 50% by 2050, from the level found in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> During the 2016 <a href="/wiki/North_American_Leaders%27_Summit" title="North American Leaders&#39; Summit">North American Leaders\' Summit</a>, the target of 50% of electricity generated from renewable sources by 2025 was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Chapultepec_Zoo_-_Jaguar_(02).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Chapultepec_Zoo_-_Jaguar_%2802%29.jpg/200px-Chapultepec_Zoo_-_Jaguar_%2802%29.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Chapultepec_Zoo_-_Jaguar_%2802%29.jpg/300px-Chapultepec_Zoo_-_Jaguar_%2802%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Chapultepec_Zoo_-_Jaguar_%2802%29.jpg/400px-Chapultepec_Zoo_-_Jaguar_%2802%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">jaguar</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Zoo" title="Chapultepec Zoo">Chapultepec Zoo</a>. The zoo is known for its success in breeding programs of <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">threatened species</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexican_wolf_lounging.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mexican_wolf_lounging.jpg/200px-Mexican_wolf_lounging.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mexican_wolf_lounging.jpg/300px-Mexican_wolf_lounging.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mexican_wolf_lounging.jpg/400px-Mexican_wolf_lounging.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1504" data-file-height="1000" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Mexican_wolf" title="Mexican wolf">Mexican wolf</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Axolote.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Axolote.jpg/200px-Axolote.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Axolote.jpg/300px-Axolote.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Axolote.jpg/400px-Axolote.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Axolotl" title="Axolotl">Axolotl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Mexico" title="Valley of Mexico">Valle de M\xc3\xa9xico</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Mexico ranks fourth<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> in the world in biodiversity and is one of the 17 <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a>. With over 200,000 different species, Mexico is home of 10\xe2\x80\x9312% of the world\'s biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-SEMARNAT_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEMARNAT-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Mexico ranks first in biodiversity in <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a> with 707 known species, second in mammals with 438 species, fourth in <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a> with 290 species, and fourth in flora, with 26,000 different species.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Mexico is also considered the second country in the world in <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> and fourth in overall species.<sup id="cite_ref-SNIB_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNIB-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> About 2,500 species are protected by Mexican legislations.<sup id="cite_ref-SNIB_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNIB-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Mexico had the second fastest rate of deforestation in the world, second only to Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2002_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2002-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The government has taken another initiative in the late 1990s to broaden the people\'s knowledge, interest and use of the country\'s esteemed biodiversity, through the <a href="/wiki/Comisi%C3%B3n_Nacional_para_el_Conocimiento_y_Uso_de_la_Biodiversidad" title="Comisi\xc3\xb3n Nacional para el Conocimiento y Uso de la Biodiversidad">Comisi\xc3\xb3n Nacional para el Conocimiento y Uso de la Biodiversidad</a>.\n</p><p>In Mexico, 170,000 square kilometres (65,637&#160;sq&#160;mi) are considered "Protected Natural Areas". These include 34 biosphere reserves (unaltered ecosystems), 67 <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Mexico" title="List of national parks of Mexico">national parks</a>, 4 natural monuments (protected in perpetuity for their aesthetic, scientific or historical value), 26 areas of protected flora and fauna, 4 areas for natural resource protection (conservation of soil, hydrological basins and forests) and 17 sanctuaries (zones rich in diverse species).<sup id="cite_ref-SEMARNAT_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEMARNAT-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The discovery of the Americas brought to the rest of the world many widely used <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">food crops</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edible_plants_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Edible plants (disambiguation)">edible plants</a>. Some of Mexico\'s native <a href="/wiki/Culinary_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Culinary art">culinary</a> ingredients include: chocolate, <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomato</a>, maize, <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guava" title="Guava">guava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chayote" title="Chayote">chayote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dysphania_ambrosioides" title="Dysphania ambrosioides">epazote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">camote</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%ADcama" class="mw-redirect" title="J\xc3\xadcama">j\xc3\xadcama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nopal" title="Nopal">nopal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zucchini" title="Zucchini">zucchini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crataegus_mexicana" title="Crataegus mexicana">tejocote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn_smut" title="Corn smut">huitlacoche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sapote" title="Sapote">sapote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamey_sapote" class="mw-redirect" title="Mamey sapote">mamey sapote</a>, many varieties of <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, and an even greater variety of <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chiles</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Habanero" title="Habanero">habanero</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jalape%C3%B1o" title="Jalape\xc3\xb1o">jalape\xc3\xb1o</a>. Most of these names come from indigenous languages like <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a>.\n</p><p>Because of its high biodiversity Mexico has also been a frequent site of <a href="/wiki/Bioprospecting" title="Bioprospecting">bioprospecting</a> by international research bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The first highly successful instance being the discovery in 1947 of the tuber "<a href="/wiki/Mexican_barbasco_trade" title="Mexican barbasco trade">Barbasco</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Dioscorea_composita" title="Dioscorea composita">Dioscorea composita</a></i>) which has a high content of <a href="/wiki/Diosgenin" title="Diosgenin">diosgenin</a>, revolutionizing the production of <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_hormones" class="mw-redirect" title="Synthetic hormones">synthetic hormones</a> in the 1950s and 1960s and eventually leading to the invention of <a href="/wiki/Combined_oral_contraceptive_pill" title="Combined oral contraceptive pill">combined oral contraceptive pills</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Mexico" title="Federal government of Mexico">Federal government of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg/220px-Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg/330px-Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg/440px-Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2502" data-file-height="2124" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto_-_World_Economic_Forum_on_Latin_America_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Pe\xc3\xb1a Nieto">Enrique Pe\xc3\xb1a Nieto</a>, President of Mexico</div></div></div>\n<p>The United Mexican States are a federation whose government is <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative</a>, democratic and <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republican</a> based on a presidential system according to the 1917 Constitution. The constitution establishes three levels of government: the federal Union, the state governments and the municipal governments. According to the constitution, all constituent states of the federation must have a republican form of government composed of three branches: the executive, represented by a governor and an appointed cabinet, the legislative branch constituted by a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mexican_state_legislatures" title="List of Mexican state legislatures">unicameral congress</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (September 2017)">original research?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the judiciary, which will include a state Supreme Court of Justice. They also have their own civil and judicial codes.\n</p><p>The federal <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_Union" title="Congress of the Union">Congress of the Union</a>, composed of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Republic_(Mexico)" title="Senate of the Republic (Mexico)">Senate of the Republic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Mexico)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Mexico)">Chamber of Deputies</a>. The Congress makes <a href="/wiki/Federal_law" title="Federal law">federal law</a>, declares war, imposes taxes, approves the national budget and international treaties, and ratifies diplomatic appointments.<sup id="cite_ref-congress_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-congress-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The federal Congress, as well as the state legislatures, are elected by a system of <a href="/wiki/Parallel_voting" title="Parallel voting">parallel voting</a> that includes plurality and <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The Chamber of Deputies has 500 deputies. Of these, 300 are elected by <a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">plurality vote</a> in <a href="/wiki/Single-member_district" title="Single-member district">single-member districts</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Federal_electoral_districts_of_Mexico" title="Federal electoral districts of Mexico">federal electoral districts</a>) and 200 are elected by proportional representation with <a href="/wiki/Closed_list" title="Closed list">closed party lists</a><sup id="cite_ref-COFIPE_congreso_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COFIPE_congreso-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> for which the country is divided into five electoral constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The Senate is made up of 128 senators. Of these, 64 senators (two for each state and two for Mexico City) are elected by plurality vote in pairs; 32 senators are the first minority or first-runner up (one for each state and one for Mexico City), and 32 are elected by proportional representation from national closed party lists.<sup id="cite_ref-COFIPE_congreso_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COFIPE_congreso-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mexico" title="President of Mexico">President of the United Mexican States</a>, who is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">government</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the Mexican military forces. The President also appoints the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Executive_Cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican Executive Cabinet">Cabinet</a> and other officers. The President is responsible for executing and enforcing the law, and has the power to <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> bills.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Suprema4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Suprema4.jpg/220px-Suprema4.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Suprema4.jpg/330px-Suprema4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Suprema4.jpg/440px-Suprema4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Suprema4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Site of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_of_the_Nation" title="Supreme Court of Justice of the Nation">Supreme Court of Justice</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The highest organ of the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial branch</a> of government is the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_of_the_Nation" title="Supreme Court of Justice of the Nation">Supreme Court of Justice</a>, the national <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court" title="Supreme court">supreme court</a>, which has eleven judges appointed by the President and approved by the Senate. The Supreme Court of Justice interprets laws and judges cases of federal competency. Other institutions of the judiciary are the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Electoral_Tribunal" title="Federal Electoral Tribunal">Federal Electoral Tribunal</a>, collegiate, unitary and district tribunals, and the Council of the Federal Judiciary.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Mexico" title="Politics of Mexico">Politics of Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Three parties have historically been the dominant parties in Mexican politics: the <a href="/wiki/National_Action_Party_(Mexico)" title="National Action Party (Mexico)">National Action Party</a>: a conservative party founded in 1939 and belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democrat_Organization_of_America" title="Christian Democrat Organization of America">Christian Democrat Organization of America</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Institutional_Revolutionary_Party" title="Institutional Revolutionary Party">Institutional Revolutionary Party</a>, a center-left party and member of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_International" title="Socialist International">Socialist International</a><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> that was founded in 1929 to unite all the factions of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a> and held an almost hegemonic power in Mexican politics since then; the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_the_Democratic_Revolution" title="Party of the Democratic Revolution">Party of the Democratic Revolution</a>: a left-wing party,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> founded in 1989 as the successor of the coalition of socialists and liberal parties.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Mexico" title="Law enforcement in Mexico">Law enforcement in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FederalPoliceDF.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/FederalPoliceDF.jpg/170px-FederalPoliceDF.jpg" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/FederalPoliceDF.jpg/255px-FederalPoliceDF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/FederalPoliceDF.jpg/340px-FederalPoliceDF.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FederalPoliceDF.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_(Mexico)" title="Federal Police (Mexico)">Federal Police</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Public security is enacted at the three levels of government, each of which has different prerogatives and responsibilities. Local and state police departments are primarily in charge of law enforcement, whereas the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Federal_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican Federal Police">Mexican Federal Police</a> are in charge of specialized duties. All levels report to the Secretar\xc3\xada de Seguridad P\xc3\xbablica (Secretary of Public Security). The General Attorney\'s Office (Procuradur\xc3\xada General de la Rep\xc3\xbablica, PGR) is the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a>\'s agency in charge of investigating and prosecuting crimes at the federal level, mainly those related to drug and arms trafficking,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> espionage, and bank robberies.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The PGR operates the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministerial_Police" title="Federal Ministerial Police">Federal Ministerial Police</a> (Policia Federal Ministerial, PMF) an investigative and preventive agency.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the government generally respects the human rights of its citizens, serious abuses of power have been reported in security operations in the southern part of the country and in indigenous communities and poor urban neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The National Human Rights Commission has had little impact in reversing this trend, engaging mostly in documentation but failing to use its powers to issue public condemnations to the officials who ignore its recommendations.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> By law, all defendants have the rights that assure them fair trials and humane treatment; however, the system is overburdened and overwhelmed with several problems.<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite the efforts of the authorities to fight crime and fraud, most Mexicans have low confidence in the police or the judicial system, and therefore, few crimes are actually reported by the citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Global Integrity Index</i> which measures the existence and effectiveness of national anti-corruption mechanisms rated Mexico 31st behind Kenya, Thailand, and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, president Calder\xc3\xb3n proposed a major reform of the judicial system, which was approved by the Congress of the Union, which included oral trials, the presumption of innocence for defendants, the authority of local police to investigate crime\xe2\x80\x94until then a prerogative of special police units\xe2\x80\x94and several other changes intended to speed up trials.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Mexico" title="Crime in Mexico">Crime in Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Drug_War" title="Mexican Drug War">Mexican Drug War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Mexico" title="Human trafficking in Mexico">Human trafficking in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Drug cartels are a major concern in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-Cartel_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cartel-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Mexico\'s drug war has left over 60,000 dead and perhaps another 20,000 missing.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The Mexican <a href="/wiki/Drug_cartel" title="Drug cartel">drug cartels</a> have as many as 100,000 members.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Mexico\'s <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Estad%C3%ADstica_y_Geograf%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Instituto Nacional de Estad\xc3\xadstica y Geograf\xc3\xada">National Geography and Statistics Institute</a> estimated that in 2014, one-fifth of Mexicans were victims of some sort of crime.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>President <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Felipe Calder\xc3\xb3n">Felipe Calder\xc3\xb3n</a> made abating organized crime one of the top priorities of his administration by deploying military personnel to cities where drug cartels operate. This move was criticized by the opposition parties and the National Human Rights Commission for escalating the violence, but its effects have been positively evaluated by the US State Department\'s <a href="/wiki/Bureau_for_International_Narcotics_and_Law_Enforcement_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Bureau for International Narcotics and Law Enforcement Affairs">Bureau for International Narcotics and Law Enforcement Affairs</a> as having obtained "unprecedented results" with "many important successes".<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since President Felipe Calder\xc3\xb3n launched a crackdown against cartels in 2006, more than 28,000 alleged criminals have been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Of the total drug-related violence 4% are innocent people,<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> mostly by-passers and people trapped in between shootings; 90% accounts for criminals and 6% for military personnel and police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In October 2007, President Calder\xc3\xb3n and US president <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> announced the <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida_Initiative" title="M\xc3\xa9rida Initiative">M\xc3\xa9rida Initiative</a>, a plan of law enforcement cooperation between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>More than 100 journalists and <a href="/wiki/List_of_journalists_and_media_workers_killed_in_Mexico" title="List of journalists and media workers killed in Mexico">media workers have been killed or disappeared</a> since 2000, and most of these crimes remained unsolved, improperly investigated, and with few perpetrators arrested and convicted.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2014_Iguala_mass_kidnapping" title="2014 Iguala mass kidnapping">mass kidnapping</a> of the 43 students in <a href="/wiki/Iguala" title="Iguala">Iguala</a> on September 26, 2014 triggered a nationwide protests against the government\xe2\x80\x99s weak response to the disappearance.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg/220px-The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg/330px-The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg/440px-The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2106" data-file-height="1550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Three_Amigos_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Pe\xc3\xb1a Nieto with Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a> of Canada and President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> of the United States at the 2016 <a href="/wiki/North_American_Leaders%27_Summit" title="North American Leaders&#39; Summit">North American Leaders\' Summit</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Mexico" title="Foreign relations of Mexico">Foreign relations of Mexico</a></div>\n<p>The foreign relations of Mexico are directed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mexico" title="President of Mexico">President of Mexico</a><sup id="cite_ref-CPEUM89_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPEUM89-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and managed through the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Mexico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Mexico)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SRE_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRE-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The principles of the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> are constitutionally recognized in the Article 89, Section 10, which include: respect for <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">legal equality of states</a>, their <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>, trend to <a href="/wiki/Non-interventionism" title="Non-interventionism">non-interventionism</a> in the domestic affairs of other countries, <a href="/wiki/Dispute_resolution" title="Dispute resolution">peaceful resolution of conflicts</a>, and promotion of <a href="/wiki/International_security" title="International security">collective security</a> through active participation in <a href="/wiki/International_organizations" class="mw-redirect" title="International organizations">international organizations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPEUM89_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPEUM89-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1930s, the <a href="/wiki/Estrada_Doctrine" title="Estrada Doctrine">Estrada Doctrine</a> has served as a crucial complement to these principles.<sup id="cite_ref-estradadoctrine_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estradadoctrine-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico is one of the founding members of several international organizations, most notably the United Nations,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Vel\xc3\xa1zquez_Flores_2007,_p._145_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vel\xc3\xa1zquez_Flores_2007,_p._145-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/OPANAL" title="OPANAL">OPANAL</a><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Group" title="Rio Group">Rio Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Mexico contributed over 40 million <a href="/wiki/American_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="American dollar">dollars</a> to the United Nations regular budget.<sup id="cite_ref-unbudget_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unbudget-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> In addition, it was the only Latin American member of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> since it joined in 1994 until <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> gained  full membership in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico is considered a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a><sup id="cite_ref-regionalpower_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regionalpower-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-regionalpower2_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regionalpower2-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> hence its presence in major economic groups such as the <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a> and the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G-20</a>. In addition, since the 1990s Mexico has sought a <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Reform of the United Nations Security Council">reform of the United Nations Security Council and its working methods</a><sup id="cite_ref-Foreign_Affairs_2005_p._215_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foreign_Affairs_2005_p._215-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> with the support of Canada, Italy, Pakistan and other nine countries, which form a group informally called the <a href="/wiki/Coffee_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Coffee Club">Coffee Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coffeeclub_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coffeeclub-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence of Mexico">War of Independence</a>, the relations of Mexico were focused primarily on the United States, its northern neighbor, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mexico" title="Economy of Mexico">largest trading partner</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> and the most <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">powerful actor in hemispheric and world affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Mexico supported the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban government</a> since its establishment in the early 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-keller_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keller-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front" title="Sandinista National Liberation Front">Sandinista revolution</a> in Nicaragua during the late 1970s,<sup id="cite_ref-salaverry_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salaverry-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> and leftist revolutionary groups in <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> during the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-elsalvador_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elsalvador-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Felipe Calder\xc3\xb3n">Felipe Calder\xc3\xb3n</a>\'s administration put a greater emphasis on relations with Latin America and the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-Calderon_FP_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calderon_FP-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Armed_Forces" title="Mexican Armed Forces">Mexican Armed Forces</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg/170px-Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg/255px-Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg/340px-Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="2100" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marina-Panther-Unitasgold2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Navy" title="Mexican Navy">Mexican Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurocopter">Eurocopter</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Mexican Armed Forces have two branches: the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Army" title="Mexican Army">Mexican Army</a> (which includes the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Air_Force" title="Mexican Air Force">Mexican Air Force</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Navy" title="Mexican Navy">Mexican Navy</a>. The Mexican Armed Forces maintain significant infrastructure, including facilities for design, research, and testing of weapons, vehicles, aircraft, naval vessels, defense systems and electronics;<sup id="cite_ref-impreso.milenio.com_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impreso.milenio.com-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mexican_Naval_missile_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mexican_Naval_missile-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> military industry manufacturing centers for building such systems, and advanced naval dockyards that build heavy military vessels and advanced missile technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marina_Michoac%C3%A1n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Marina_Michoac%C3%A1n.jpg/220px-Marina_Michoac%C3%A1n.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/Marina_Michoac%C3%A1n.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="212" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marina_Michoac%C3%A1n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mexican built <a href="/wiki/Sierra-class_corvette" title="Sierra-class corvette">Sierra-class corvettes</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In recent years, Mexico has improved its training techniques, military command and information structures and has taken steps to becoming more self-reliant in supplying its military by designing as well as manufacturing its own arms,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> missiles,<sup id="cite_ref-Mexican_Naval_missile_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mexican_Naval_missile-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> aircraft,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> vehicles, heavy weaponry, electronics,<sup id="cite_ref-impreso.milenio.com_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impreso.milenio.com-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> defense systems,<sup id="cite_ref-impreso.milenio.com_159-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impreso.milenio.com-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> armor, heavy military industrial equipment and heavy naval vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1990s, when the military escalated its role in the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Drug_War" title="Mexican Drug War">war on drugs</a>, increasing importance has been placed on acquiring airborne surveillance platforms, aircraft, <a href="/wiki/Helicopters" class="mw-redirect" title="Helicopters">helicopters</a>, digital war-fighting technologies,<sup id="cite_ref-impreso.milenio.com_159-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impreso.milenio.com-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> urban warfare equipment and rapid troop transport.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico has the capabilities to manufacture nuclear weapons, but abandoned this possibility with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tlatelolco" title="Treaty of Tlatelolco">Treaty of Tlatelolco</a> in 1968 and pledged to only use its nuclear technology for peaceful purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> In 1970, Mexico\'s national institute for nuclear research successfully refined weapons grade uranium<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (March 2011)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> which is used in the manufacture of nuclear weapons but in April 2010, Mexico agreed to turn over its weapons grade uranium to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Historically, Mexico has remained neutral in international conflicts,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mexico_in_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexico in World War II">with the exception of World War II</a>. However, in recent years some political parties have proposed an amendment of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico" title="Constitution of Mexico">Constitution</a> to allow the Mexican Army, Air Force or Navy to collaborate with the United Nations in <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping missions</a>, or to provide military help to countries that officially ask for it.<sup id="cite_ref-neutral_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neutral-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Mexico" title="Administrative divisions of Mexico">Administrative divisions of Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/States_of_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="States of Mexico">States of Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Mexico" title="Municipalities of Mexico">Municipalities of Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mexican_state_legislatures" title="List of Mexican state legislatures">List of Mexican state legislatures</a></div>\n<p>The United Mexican States are a federation of 31 free and sovereign states, which form a union that exercises a degree of jurisdiction over Mexico City and other <a href="/wiki/Territory_(administrative_division)" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory (administrative division)">territories</a>.\n</p><p>Each state has its own constitution, <a href="/wiki/Congress" title="Congress">congress</a>, and a judiciary, and its citizens elect by <a href="/wiki/Direct_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct vote">direct voting</a> a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mexican_state_governors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Mexican state governors">governor</a> for a six-year term, and representatives to their respective unicameral state congresses for three-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico City is a special political division that belongs to the federation as a whole and not to a particular state. Formerly known as the Federal District, its autonomy was previously limited relative to that of the states.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> It dropped this designation in 2016 and is in the process of achieving greater political autonomy by becoming a federal entity with <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Assembly_of_Mexico_City" title="Constitutional Assembly of Mexico City">its own constitution</a> and congress.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The states are divided into <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Mexico" title="Municipalities of Mexico">municipalities</a>, the smallest administrative political entity in the country, governed by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor or municipal president</a> (<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">presidente municipal</i>), elected by its residents by plurality.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" title="Zacatecas">Zacatecas (ZAC)</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Zacatecas_City" title="Zacatecas City">Zacatecas</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mexico" title="Economy of Mexico">Economy of Mexico</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Mexico" title="Economic history of Mexico">Economic history of Mexico</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;" colspan="2">Share of world GDP (PPP)<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Share\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1980</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">3.06%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1990</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.68%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2000\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.53%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2010\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">2.02%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2017</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.94%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1107" data-file-height="862" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexico_Product_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Mexico\'s exports. The country has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_complexity" title="List of countries by economic complexity">most complex economy</a> in Latin America.</div></div></div>\n<p>Mexico has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">15th largest</a> nominal GDP and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">11th largest</a> by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. GDP annual average growth for the period of 1995\xe2\x80\x932002 was 5.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-Crandall_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crandall-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Mexico\'s Gross Domestic Product (GDP) in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) was estimated at US $2.2602 trillion in 2015, and $1.3673 trillion in nominal exchange rates.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Mexico\'s GDP in PPP per capita was US $18,714.05. The World Bank reported in 2009 that the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_National_Income" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross National Income">Gross National Income</a> in market exchange rates was the second highest in Latin America, after <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> at US $1,830.392&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-GNI_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GNI-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> which lead to the highest <a href="/wiki/Gross_National_Income" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross National Income">income per capita</a> in the region at $15,311.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GNIPC_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GNIPC-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Mexico is now firmly established as an upper middle-income country. After the slowdown of 2001 the country has recovered and has grown 4.2, 3.0 and 4.8 percent in 2004, 2005 and 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> even though it is considered to be well below Mexico\'s potential growth.<sup id="cite_ref-Hufbauer_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hufbauer-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, after the 2008\xe2\x80\x932009 recession, the economy grew an average of 3.32 percent per year from 2010 to 2014.\n</p><p>From the late 1990s onwards, the majority of the population has been considered to be part of the growing middle class by international economic organizations<sup id="cite_ref-WB_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> but according to Mexico\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Council_for_the_Evaluation_of_Social_Development_Policy_(CONEVAL)" title="National Council for the Evaluation of Social Development Policy (CONEVAL)">National Council for the Evaluation of Social Development Policy</a> (CONEVAL) from 2006 to 2010 the portion of the population who lives in poverty rose from 18%-19%<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> to 46% (52 million people).<sup id="cite_ref-CONEVAL_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONEVAL-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> However, rather than Mexico\'s economy crashing, international economists attribute the huge increase in the percentage of population living below the country\'s poverty line to the CONEVAL using new, multidimensional standards to define it, as now besides people who lives below the economic welfare line, people who lacks at least one "social need" such as complete education, access to healthcare, access to regular food, housing services and goods, social security etc. were considered to be living in poverty (several countries do collect information regarding the persistence of said vulnerabilities on their population, but Mexico is the only one that classifies people with one or more of those carencies as living below it\'s national poverty line).
