Said economists do point out that the percentage of people living in poverty according Mexico\'s national poverty line is around 40 times higher than the one reported by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank\'s</a> international poverty line (with said difference being the biggest in the world) and ponder if it wouldn\'t be better for countries in the situation of Mexico to adopt internationalized standards to measure poverty so the numbers obtained could be used to make accurate international comparisons.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>\'s own poverty line (defined as the percentage of a country\'s population who earns half or less of the national median income) 21.5% of Mexico\'s population lives in situation of poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-OECDREFORMA_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECDREFORMA-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Among the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> countries, Mexico has the second highest degree of economic disparity between the extremely poor and extremely rich, after Chile&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 although it has been falling over the last decade, being only one of few countries in which this is the case.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The bottom ten percent in the income hierarchy disposes of 1.36% of the country\'s resources, whereas the upper ten percent dispose of almost 36%. OECD also notes that Mexico\'s budgeted expenses for poverty alleviation and social development is only about a third of the OECD average \xe2\x80\x93 both in absolute and relative numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-OECDREFORMA_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECDREFORMA-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> This is also reflected by the fact that infant mortality in Mexico is three times higher than the average among OECD nations whereas it\'s literacy levels are in the median range of OECD nations. Nevertheless, according to <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, by 2050 Mexico will have the 5th largest economy in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, according to <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a>, by 2050 Mexico will have the 5th largest economy in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a 2008 UN report the average income in a typical urbanized area of Mexico was $26,654, while the average income in rural areas just miles away was only $8,403.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Daily minimum wages are set annually being set at $80.04 <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">Mexican pesos</a> ($4.5 USD) in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The electronics industry of Mexico has grown enormously within the last decade. Mexico has the sixth largest electronics industry in the world after <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Mexico is the second largest exporter of electronics to the United States where it exported $71.4 billion worth of electronics in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-prnewswire.com_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire.com-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The Mexican electronics industry is dominated by the manufacture and OEM design of televisions, displays, computers, mobile phones, circuit boards, semiconductors, electronic appliances, communications equipment and LCD modules. The Mexican electronics industry grew 20% between 2010 and 2011, up from its constant growth rate of 17% between 2003 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-prnewswire.com_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire.com-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Currently electronics represent 30% of Mexico\'s exports.<sup id="cite_ref-prnewswire.com_193-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prnewswire.com-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico produces the most automobiles of any North American nation.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The industry produces technologically complex components and engages in some research and development activities.<sup id="cite_ref-Gereffi_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gereffi-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The "Big Three" (<a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford">Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a>) have been operating in Mexico since the 1930s, while <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> built their plants in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-Hufbauer_Auto_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hufbauer_Auto-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Puebla,_Puebla" class="mw-redirect" title="Puebla, Puebla">Puebla</a> alone, 70 industrial part-makers cluster around Volkswagen.<sup id="cite_ref-Gereffi_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gereffi-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> In the 2010s expansion of the sector was surging. In 2014 alone, more than $10 billion in investment was committed. In September 2016 Kia motors opened a $1 billion factory in <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Le%C3%B3n" title="Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n">Nuevo Le\xc3\xb3n</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> with Audi also opening an assembling plant in Puebla the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> currently have plants in constructuion.<sup id="cite_ref-KiaMexico_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KiaMexico-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The domestic car industry is represented by <a href="/wiki/DINA_S.A." title="DINA S.A.">DINA S.A.</a>, which has built buses and trucks since 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> and the new <a href="/wiki/Mastretta" title="Mastretta">Mastretta</a> company that builds the high-performance <a href="/wiki/Mastretta_MXT" title="Mastretta MXT">Mastretta MXT</a> sports car.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, trade with the United States and Canada accounted for almost 50% of Mexico\'s exports and 45% of its imports.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> During the first three quarters of 2010, the United States had a $46.0 billion <a href="/wiki/Trade_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade deficit">trade deficit</a> with Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> In August 2010 Mexico surpassed France to become the 9th largest holder of US debt.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The commercial and financial dependence on the US is a cause for concern.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The remittances from Mexican citizens working in the United States account for 0.2% of Mexico\'s GDP<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> which was equal to US$20 billion per year in 2004 and is the tenth largest source of foreign income after oil, industrial exports, manufactured goods, electronics, heavy industry, automobiles, construction, food, banking and financial services.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> According to Mexico\'s central bank, remittances in 2008 amounted to $25bn.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Mexico" title="Telecommunications in Mexico">Telecommunications in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MORELOS_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/MORELOS_3.jpg/200px-MORELOS_3.jpg" width="200" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/MORELOS_3.jpg/300px-MORELOS_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/MORELOS_3.jpg/400px-MORELOS_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1385" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MORELOS_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Morelos 3, the latest addition to the <a href="/wiki/Morelos_Satellite_System" title="Morelos Satellite System">Morelos Satellite System</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The telecommunications industry is mostly dominated by <a href="/wiki/Telmex" title="Telmex">Telmex</a> (<i>Tel\xc3\xa9fonos de M\xc3\xa9xico</i>), privatized in 1990. By 2006, Telmex had expanded its operations to Colombia, Peru, Chile, Argentina, Brazil and Uruguay and the United States. Other players in the domestic industry are <a href="/wiki/Axtel" title="Axtel">Axtel</a> and Maxcom. Because of Mexican <a href="/wiki/Orography" title="Orography">orography</a>, providing a landline telephone service at remote mountainous areas is expensive, and the penetration of line-phones per capita is low compared to other Latin American countries, at 40 percent; however, 82% of Mexicans over the age of 14 own a mobile phone. Mobile telephony has the advantage of reaching all areas at a lower cost, and the total number of mobile lines is almost two times that of landlines, with an estimation of 63 million lines.<sup id="cite_ref-ciacom_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciacom-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The telecommunication industry is regulated by the government through <a href="/wiki/Cofetel" class="mw-redirect" title="Cofetel">Cofetel</a> (<i>Comisi\xc3\xb3n Federal de Telecomunicaciones</i>).\n</p><p>The Mexican satellite system is domestic and operates 120 earth stations. There is also extensive microwave radio relay network and considerable use of fiber-optic and coaxial cable.<sup id="cite_ref-ciacom_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciacom-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Mexican satellites are operated by <i>Sat\xc3\xa9lites Mexicanos</i> (<a href="/wiki/Satmex" title="Satmex">Satmex</a>), a private company, leader in Latin America and servicing both North and South America.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> It offers broadcast, telephone and telecommunication services to 37 countries in the Americas, from Canada to <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>. Through business partnerships Satmex provides high-speed connectivity to ISPs and Digital Broadcast Services.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Satmex maintains its own satellite fleet with most of the fleet being designed and built in Mexico.\n</p><p>Major players in the broadcasting industry are <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a>, the largest Mexican media company in the Spanish-speaking world,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TV_Azteca" title="TV Azteca">TV Azteca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imagen_Televisi%C3%B3n" title="Imagen Televisi\xc3\xb3n">Imagen Televisi\xc3\xb3n</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Mexico" title="Electricity sector in Mexico">Electricity sector in Mexico</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I,_Fase_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg/200px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg/300px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg/400px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_Central_E%C3%B3lica_Sureste_I%2C_Fase_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1654" data-file-height="1104" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Central E\xc3\xb3lica Sureste I, Fase II in Oaxaca. The Isthmus of Tehuantepec is the region of Mexico with the highest capacity for wind energy. (see <i><a href="/wiki/Tehuantepecer" title="Tehuantepecer">Tehuantepecer</a></i>, a strong wind that affects the region)</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III,_Fase_1._(21526244958).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg/200px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg/300px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg/400px-Inauguraci%C3%B3n_de_la_Central_Geotermoel%C3%A9ctrica_Azufres_III%2C_Fase_1._%2821526244958%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5520" data-file-height="3680" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Central Geotermoel\xc3\xa9ctrica Azufres III in Michoac\xc3\xa1n. 100% of the electricity produced in Michoac\xc3\xa1n comes from renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-Geothermal_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geothermal-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> 90% comes from <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric plants">hydroelectric plants</a>, and 10% from the Azufres <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">Geothermal</a> Field.<sup id="cite_ref-Geothermal_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geothermal-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Energy production in Mexico is managed by the state-owned companies <a href="/wiki/Comisi%C3%B3n_Federal_de_Electricidad" title="Comisi\xc3\xb3n Federal de Electricidad">Federal Commission of Electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pemex" title="Pemex">Pemex</a>.\n</p><p>Pemex, the public company in charge of exploration, extraction, transportation and marketing of crude oil and natural gas, as well as the refining and distribution of petroleum products and petrochemicals, is one of the largest companies in the world by revenue, making US $86 billion in sales a year.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fortune_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Mexico is the sixth-largest oil producer in the world, with 3.7 million barrels per day.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> In 1980 oil exports accounted for 61.6% of total exports; by 2000 it was only 7.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-Gereffi_195-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gereffi-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest hydro plant in Mexico is the 2,400 MW <a href="/wiki/Chicoas%C3%A9n_Dam" title="Chicoas\xc3\xa9n Dam">Manuel Moreno Torres Dam</a> in Chicoas\xc3\xa9n, <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Grijalva_River" title="Grijalva River">Grijalva River</a>. This is the world\'s fourth most productive hydroelectric plant.<sup id="cite_ref-EIA_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico is the country with the world\'s third largest solar potential.<sup id="cite_ref-S&amp;G_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S&amp;G-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The country\'s gross solar potential is estimated at 5kWh/m2 daily, which corresponds to 50 times national electricity generation.<sup id="cite_ref-ER_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ER-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Currently, there is over 1 million square meters of <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar thermal">solar thermal</a> panels<sup id="cite_ref-SENER_2009b_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SENER_2009b-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> installed in Mexico, while in 2005, there were 115,000 square meters of <a href="/wiki/Solar_PV" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar PV">solar PV</a> (photo-voltaic). It is expected that in 2012 there will be 1,8 million square meters of installed solar thermal panels.<sup id="cite_ref-SENER_2009b_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SENER_2009b-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The project named <a href="/wiki/SEGH-CFE_1" title="SEGH-CFE 1">SEGH-CFE 1</a>, located in Puerto Libertad, Sonora, Northwest of Mexico, will have capacity of 46.8 MW from an array of 187,200 solar panels when complete in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Sonora_Energy_Group_Hermosillo_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sonora_Energy_Group_Hermosillo-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> All of the electricity will be sold directly to the CFE and absorbed into the utility\'s transmission system for distribution throughout their existing network. At an installed capacity of 46.8 MWp, when complete in 2013, the project will be the first utility scale project of its kind in Mexico and the largest solar project of any kind in Latin America.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_Mexico" title="History of science and technology in Mexico">History of science and technology in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Autonomous_University_of_Mexico" title="National Autonomous University of Mexico">National Autonomous University of Mexico</a> was officially established in 1910,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> and the university became one of the most important institutes of higher learning in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-page285_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page285-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> UNAM provides world class education in science, medicine, and engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Many scientific institutes and new institutes of higher learning, such as <a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="National Polytechnic Institute">National Polytechnic Institute</a> (founded in 1936),<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> were established during the first half of the 20th century. Most of the new research institutes were created within UNAM. Twelve institutes were integrated into UNAM from 1929 to 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-page18_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page18-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> In 1959, the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Mexican Academy of Sciences">Mexican Academy of Sciences</a> was created to coordinate scientific efforts between academics.\n</p><p>In 1995, the Mexican chemist <a href="/wiki/Mario_J._Molina" title="Mario J. Molina">Mario J. Molina</a> shared the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a> with <a href="/wiki/Paul_J._Crutzen" title="Paul J. Crutzen">Paul J. Crutzen</a> and <a href="/wiki/F._Sherwood_Rowland" title="F. Sherwood Rowland">F. Sherwood Rowland</a> for their work in atmospheric chemistry, particularly concerning the formation and decomposition of ozone.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Molina, an alumnus of UNAM, became the first Mexican citizen to win the Nobel Prize in science.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In recent years, the largest scientific project being developed in Mexico was the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Large_Millimeter_Telescope" title="Large Millimeter Telescope">Large Millimeter Telescope</a> (Gran Telescopio Milim\xc3\xa9trico, GMT), the world\'s largest and most sensitive single-aperture telescope in its frequency range.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> It was designed to observe regions of space obscured by stellar dust.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Mexico" title="Tourism in Mexico">Tourism in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg/220px-Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg/330px-Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg/440px-Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Calle_del_centro_de_morelia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Street in the historic center of <a href="/wiki/Morelia" title="Morelia">Morelia</a>. Mexico has historical architecture in most of its towns being the country with the highest number of Colonial buildings and structures in all of the Americas and also placing a vast number of Pre-colonial monuments.</div></div></div>\n<p>Mexico has traditionally been among the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">most visited countries in the world</a> according to the World Tourism Organization and it is the most visited country in the Americas after the United States. The most notable attractions are the <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesoamerican">Mesoamerican</a> ruins, cultural festivals, colonial cities, nature reserves and the beach resorts. The nation\'s wide range of climates, from temperate to tropical, and unique culture \xe2\x80\x93 a fusion of the European and the Mesoamerican \xe2\x80\x93 make Mexico an attractive destination. The peak tourism seasons in the country are during December and the mid-Summer, with brief surges during the week before <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spring_break" title="Spring break">Spring break</a>, when many of the beach resort sites become popular destinations for college students from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.\n</p><p>As of 2017, Mexico was the 6th most visited country in the world and  had the 15th highest income from tourism in the world which is also the highest in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-WTO_Tourism_Highlights_2018_Edition_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTO_Tourism_Highlights_2018_Edition-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> The vast majority of tourists come to Mexico from the United States and Canada followed by Europe and Asia. A smaller number also come from other Latin American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> In the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Travel_and_Tourism_Competitiveness_Report" title="Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report">Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report</a>, Mexico was ranked 22nd in the world, which was 3rd in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The coastlines of Mexico harbor many stretches of beaches that are frequented by sunbathers and other visitors. <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico#Article_27" title="Constitution of Mexico">According to national law</a>, the entirety of the coastlines are under federal ownership, that is, all beaches in the country are <a href="/wiki/Public_property" title="Public property">public</a>. On the Yucat\xc3\xa1n peninsula, one of the most popular beach destinations is the resort town of <a href="/wiki/Canc%C3%BAn" title="Canc\xc3\xban">Canc\xc3\xban</a>, especially among <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">students</a> during <a href="/wiki/Spring_break" title="Spring break">spring break</a>. Just offshore is the beach island of <a href="/wiki/Isla_Mujeres" title="Isla Mujeres">Isla Mujeres</a>, and to the east is the <a href="/wiki/Isla_Holbox" title="Isla Holbox">Isla Holbox</a>. To the south of Cancun is the coastal strip called <a href="/wiki/Riviera_Maya" title="Riviera Maya">Riviera Maya</a> which includes the beach town of <a href="/wiki/Playa_del_Carmen" title="Playa del Carmen">Playa del Carmen</a> and the ecological parks of <a href="/wiki/Xcaret" title="Xcaret">Xcaret</a> and Xel-H\xc3\xa1. A day trip to the south of Canc\xc3\xban is the historic port of <a href="/wiki/Tulum" title="Tulum">Tulum</a>. In addition to its beaches, the town of Tulum is notable for its cliff-side <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayan</a> ruins.\n</p><p>On the <a href="/wiki/Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific">Pacific</a> coast is the notable tourist destination of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>. Once the destination for the rich and famous, the beaches have become crowded and the shores are now home to many multi-story hotels and vendors. Acapulco is home to renowned cliff divers: trained divers who leap from the side of a vertical cliff into the surf below.\n</p><p>At the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a> is the resort town of <a href="/wiki/Cabo_San_Lucas" title="Cabo San Lucas">Cabo San Lucas</a>, a town noted for its beaches and <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">marlin</a> <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Further north along the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Cort%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea of Cort\xc3\xa9s">Sea of Cort\xc3\xa9s</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_Concepci%C3%B3n,_Baja_California_Sur" title="Bah\xc3\xada Concepci\xc3\xb3n, Baja California Sur">Bah\xc3\xada de La Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a>, another beach town known for its sports fishing. Closer to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> border is the weekend draw of <a href="/wiki/San_Felipe,_Baja_California" title="San Felipe, Baja California">San Felipe, Baja California</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Mexico" title="Transportation in Mexico">Transportation in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg/250px-Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg/375px-Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg/500px-Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_Baluarte_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Baluarte_Bridge" title="Baluarte Bridge">Baluarte Bridge</a> is the highest cable-stayed bridge in the world, the fifth-highest bridge overall and the highest bridge in the Americas.</div></div></div>\n<p>The roadway network in Mexico is extensive and all areas in the country are covered by it.<sup id="cite_ref-nations_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nations-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> The roadway network in Mexico has an extent of 366,095&#160;km (227,481&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-sctroad_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sctroad-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> of which 116,802&#160;km (72,577&#160;mi) are paved,<sup id="cite_ref-sctroad-2_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sctroad-2-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> making it the largest paved-roadway network in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Of these, 10,474&#160;km (6,508&#160;mi) are multi-lane <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">expressways</a>: 9,544&#160;km (5,930&#160;mi) are four-lane highways and the rest have 6 or more lanes.<sup id="cite_ref-sctroad-2_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sctroad-2-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico was one of the first Latin American countries to promote railway development,<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> and the network covers 30,952&#160;km (19,233&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-encnations_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnations-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_Communications_and_Transportation_(Mexico)" title="Secretariat of Communications and Transportation (Mexico)">Secretary of Communications and Transport</a> of Mexico proposed a high-speed rail link that will transport its passengers from <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-azcentral.com_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azcentral.com-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> The train, which will travel at 300 kilometres per hour (190 miles per hour),<sup id="cite_ref-systra.com_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-systra.com-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> will allow passengers to travel from Mexico City to Guadalajara in just 2&#160;hours.<sup id="cite_ref-systra.com_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-systra.com-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> The whole project was projected to cost 240&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/MXN" class="mw-redirect" title="MXN">pesos</a>, or about 25&#160;billion US$<sup id="cite_ref-azcentral.com_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azcentral.com-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> and is being paid for jointly by the Mexican government and the local private sector including the wealthiest man in the world, Mexico\'s billionaire business tycoon <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Slim" title="Carlos Slim">Carlos Slim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> The government of the state of <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Yucat\xc3\xa1n</a> is also funding the construction of a high speed line connecting the cities of <a href="/wiki/Cozumel" title="Cozumel">Cozumel</a> to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="M\xc3\xa9rida, Yucat\xc3\xa1n">M\xc3\xa9rida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chichen_Itza" title="Chichen Itza">Chichen Itza</a> and Canc\xc3\xban.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mexico has 233 airports with paved runways; of these, 35 carry 97% of the passenger traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-encnations_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnations-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport" title="Mexico City International Airport">Mexico City International Airport</a> remains the busiest in Latin America and the 36th busiest in the world<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> transporting 45 million passengers a year..<sup id="cite_ref-aicmstats_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aicmstats-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Mexico" title="Water supply and sanitation in Mexico">Water supply and sanitation in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Among the achievements is a significant increase in access to piped water supply in urban areas (88% to 93%) as well as in rural areas (50% to 74%) between 1990 and 2010. Additionally, a strong nationwide increase in access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">improved sanitation</a> (64% to 85%) was observed in the same period. Other achievements include the existence of a functioning national system to finance water and sanitation infrastructure with a National Water Commission as its apex institution; and the existence of a few well-performing utilities such as Aguas y Drenaje de Monterrey.\n</p><p>The challenges include water scarcity in the northern and central parts of the country; inadequate water service quality (drinking water quality; 11% of Mexicans receiving water only intermittently as of 2014);<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> poor technical and commercial efficiency of most utilities (with an average level of <a href="/wiki/Non-revenue_water" title="Non-revenue water">non-revenue water</a> of 43.2% in 2010);<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> an insufficient share of wastewater receiving treatment (36% in 2006); and still inadequate access in rural areas. In addition to on-going investments to expand access, the government has embarked on a large investment program to improve wastewater treatment.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mexico" title="Demographics of Mexico">Demographics of Mexico</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical population</th></tr><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">\xc2\xb1%</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1910 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">15,160,369</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x80\x94&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1921 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">14,334,780</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x925.4%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1940 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">19,653,552</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+37.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1960 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">34,923,129</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+77.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1980 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">66,846,833</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+91.4%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">97,483,412</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+45.8%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2015 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">121,005,816</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+24.1%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: <a href="/wiki/INEGI" class="mw-redirect" title="INEGI">INEGI</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Throughout the 19th century, the population of Mexico had barely doubled. This trend continued during the first two decades of the 20th century, and even in the 1920 census there was a loss of about 2 million inhabitants. The phenomenon can be explained because during the decade from 1910 to 1920 the Mexican Revolution took place.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Mexiko_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>The growth rate increased dramatically between the 1930s and the 1980s, when the country registered growth rates of over 3% (1950\xe2\x80\x931980). The Mexican population doubled in twenty years, and at that rate it was expected that by the year 2000 there would be 120 million Mexicans. Life expectancy went from 36 years (in 1895) to 72 years (in the year 2000).\n</p><p>According to estimations made by Mexico\'s <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Estad%C3%ADstica_y_Geograf%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Instituto Nacional de Estad\xc3\xadstica y Geograf\xc3\xada">National Geography and Statistics Institute</a>, as of 2017 Mexico has 123.5 million inhabitants<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> making it the most populous Spanish-speaking country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Spanishhistory_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spanishhistory-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> Between 2005 and 2010, the Mexican population grew at an average of 1.70% per year, up from 1.16% per year between 2000 and 2005.\n</p><p>Even though Mexico is a very ethnically diverse country, research about ethnicity has largely been a forgotten field, in consequence of the post-revolutionary efforts of Mexico\'s government to unify all non-indigenous Mexicans under a single ethnic identity (that of the "Mestizo"). As a result, since 1930 the only explicit ethnic classification that has been included in Mexican censuses has been that of "Indigenous peoples".<sup id="cite_ref-EL_MESTIZAJE_Y_LAS_CULTURAS_REGIONALES_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EL_MESTIZAJE_Y_LAS_CULTURAS_REGIONALES-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Even then, across the years the government has used different criteria to count Indigenous peoples, with each of them returning considerably different numbers. It is not until very recently that the Mexican government begun conducting surveys that considered the <a href="/wiki/Afro-Mexican" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Mexican">Afro-Mexican</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexicans_of_European_descent" title="Mexicans of European descent">Euro-Mexican</a> population that lives in the country.\n</p><p>As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it is estimated that 1.2 million foreigners have settled in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-UN2017_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN2017-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> up from nearly 1 million in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The vast majority of migrants come from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (900,000), making Mexico the top destination for <a href="/wiki/American_immigration_to_Mexico" title="American immigration to Mexico">U.S. citizens abroad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> The second largest group comes from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> (54,500), followed by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (27,600).<sup id="cite_ref-UN2017_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN2017-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Other major sources of migration are fellow Latin American countries, which include <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (20,600), <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> (19,200) and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> (18,100).<sup id="cite_ref-UN2017_251-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN2017-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Historically, the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Mexicans" title="Lebanese Mexicans">Lebanese diaspora</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Mexico" title="Mennonites in Mexico">German-born Mennonite migration</a> have left a notorious impact in the country\'s culture, particularly in its cuisine and traditional music.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> At the turn of the 21st century, several trends have increased the number of foreigners residing in the country such as the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932014_Spanish_financial_crisis" title="2008\xe2\x80\x932014 Spanish financial crisis">2008\xe2\x80\x932014 Spanish financial crisis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> increasing gang-related violence in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Triangle_of_Central_America" title="Northern Triangle of Central America">Northern Triangle of Central America</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Crisis_in_Venezuela" title="Crisis in Venezuela">ongoing political and economic crisis in Venezuela</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Mexico" title="Automotive industry in Mexico">automotive industry boom</a> led by Japanese and South Korean investment.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity_and_race">Ethnicity and race</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg/250px-Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg" width="250" height="409" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg/375px-Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg/500px-Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="707" data-file-height="1156" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ignacio_Mar%C3%ADa_Barreda_-_Las_castas_mexicanas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depiction of the <a href="/wiki/Casta" title="Casta">casta</a> system in Mexico. Painting of 1777.</div></div></div>\n<p>Mexico is ethnically diverse; with people of several ethnicities being united under a single national identity.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated115_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated115-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> The core part of Mexican national identity is formed on the basis of a synthesis of cultures, primarily European culture and indigenous cultures, in a process known as <a href="/wiki/Mestizaje" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizaje">mestizaje</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated115_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated115-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-census_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> Mexican politicians and reformers such as <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vasconcelos" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos">Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos</a> (promoter of the <i><a href="/wiki/La_Raza_C%C3%B3smica" class="mw-redirect" title="La Raza C\xc3\xb3smica">cosmic race</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Gamio" title="Manuel Gamio">Manuel Gamio</a> (promoter of <i><a href="/wiki/Indigenismo" title="Indigenismo">indigenismo</a></i>) were instrumental in building a Mexican national identity on the concept of mestizaje.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight,_Alan_1990._pp._78_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight,_Alan_1990._pp._78-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The large majority of Mexicans have historically been classified as "<a href="/wiki/Mestizos_in_Mexico" title="Mestizos in Mexico">Mestizos</a>". In modern Mexican usage, the term <i>mestizo</i> is primarily a cultural identity rather than the racial identity it was during the colonial era, resulting in individuals with varying phenotypes being classified under the same identity, regardless of whether they are of mixed ancestry or not.<sup id="cite_ref-redalyc_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-redalyc-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> In the Yucat\xc3\xa1n peninsula the word Mestizo has a different meaning, being used to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Yucatec_Maya_language" title="Yucatec Maya language">Maya</a>-speaking populations living in traditional communities, because during the <a href="/wiki/Caste_War_of_Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Caste War of Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Caste War</a> of the late 19th century those Maya who did not join the rebellion were classified as mestizos.<sup id="cite_ref-Bartolom\xc3\xa9_1996:2_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartolom\xc3\xa9_1996:2-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> In Chiapas the word "Ladino" is used instead of mestizo.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Due the different definitions and socio-cultural connotations the term has carried through history it was deemed too imprecise to be used for ethnic classification, which led to it being abandoned by the government and the Mexican society,<sup id="cite_ref-brit-mex_122-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-mex-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> with it\'s use being limited to intellectual circles. According to the Mexican census of 1921 and publications who retake it\'s results such as  <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica">Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica</a>, the majority of Mexicans (from 50% to 67% of the country\'s population) identify as Mestizo,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia_Britannica_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia_Britannica-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> although modern research has observed that when asked directly about their ethno-racial identification, many Mexicans do not identify as Mestizos.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The total percentage of Mexico\'s population who is <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Mexico" title="Indigenous peoples of Mexico">indigenous</a> varies considerably depending of the criteria used by the government on its censuses: it is 5.4% if the ability to speak an indigenous language is used as the criteria to define a person as indigenous,<sup id="cite_ref-inegiindigenous_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inegiindigenous-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> if racial self-identification is used it is 14.9%<sup id="cite_ref-CDI1_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDI1-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> and if people who consider themselves part indigenous are also included it amounts to 23%.<sup id="cite_ref-beta.inegi.org.mx_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beta.inegi.org.mx-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, all the censuses conclude that the majority of Mexico\'s indigenous population is concentrated in rural areas of the southern and south-eastern Mexican states such as<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Yucat\xc3\xa1n at 59%, Quintana Roo 39% and Campeche 27%, who are chiefly <a href="/wiki/Maya_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya people">Maya</a>; Oaxaca with 48% of the population, the most numerous groups being the <a href="/wiki/Mixtec" title="Mixtec">Mixtec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Zapotec people">Zapotec peoples</a>; Chiapas at 28%, the majority being <a href="/wiki/Tzeltal" title="Tzeltal">Tzeltal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tzotzil_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tzotzil people">Tzotzil</a> Maya; Hidalgo 24%, the majority being <a href="/wiki/Otomi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Otomi people">Otomi</a>; Puebla 19%, and Guerrero 17%, mostly <a href="/wiki/Nahua_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahua people">Nahua peoples</a> and the states of San Luis Potos\xc3\xad and Veracruz are both home to a population that is 15% indigenous, mostly from the <a href="/wiki/Totonac" title="Totonac">Totonac</a>, Nahua and <a href="/wiki/Huastec_people" title="Huastec people">Teenek (Huastec)</a> groups.<sup id="cite_ref-inegi.org.mx_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inegi.org.mx-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> The absolute numbers of the indigenous population are growing, but at a slower rate than the rest of the population so that the percentage of indigenous peoples in regards to total population is nonetheless falling.<sup id="cite_ref-CDI_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDI-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> All of the indices of social development for the indigenous population are considerably lower than the national average even though the indigenous population participates in the workforce longer than the national average with 55% of the indigenous population receiving less than a minimum salary, compared to 20% for the national average. Many practice subsistence agriculture and regulate some internal issues under <a href="/wiki/Customary_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Customary law">customary law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-inegi.org.mx_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inegi.org.mx-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Similarly to Mestizo and Indigenous peoples, estimations for the percentage of <a href="/wiki/Mexicans_of_European_descent" title="Mexicans of European descent">European-descended Mexicans</a> within the Mexican population vary considerably: according to the Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica which uses as reference the 1921 census their numbers range from around 10%\xe2\x80\x9320%<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia_Britannica_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia_Britannica-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> (the results of the 1921 census, however, have been contested by various historians and deemed innaccurate).<sup id="cite_ref-MexicoRacista1_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexicoRacista1-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> Surveys that account for different phenotypical trais (hair color, skin color etc.) however, report rather higher percentages, with it reaching 47% according a survey carried out by the Mexican government with the aim to adress ethnic discrimination in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conapred.org.mx_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conapred.org.mx-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DISC-RACIAL_2011_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC-RACIAL_2011-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup><br /> While during the colonial era, most of the European migration into Mexico was <a href="/wiki/Spaniards_in_Mexico" title="Spaniards in Mexico">Spanish</a>, in the 19th and 20th centuries a substantial number of non-Spanish Europeans immigrated to the country. According to 20th- and 21st-century academics, large scale intermixing between European immigrants and native Indigenous peoples would produce a Mestizo group which would become the overwhelming majority of Mexico\'s population by the time of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican revolution">Mexican revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fnavarrete_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fnavarrete-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> However, according to church registers from the colonial times, the majority of European men married with European women.<sup id="cite_ref-MexicoRacista1_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexicoRacista1-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> Said registers also put in question other narratives held by contemporary academics, such as European migrants who arrived to Mexico being almost exclusively men,<sup id="cite_ref-scielo.org.mx2_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scielo.org.mx2-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> or that "pure Spanish" people were all part of a small powerful elite, as Spaniards were often the most numerous ethnic group in the colonial cities<sup id="cite_ref-Ensayospoblaci\xc3\xb3nM\xc3\xa9xico_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ensayospoblaci\xc3\xb3nM\xc3\xa9xico-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> and there were menial workers and people in poverty who were of complete Spanish origin.<sup id="cite_ref-scielo.org.mx2_283-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scielo.org.mx2-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> Nowadays Mexico\'s northern and western regions have the highest European populations, with the majority of the people not having native admixture or being of predominantly European ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-UnitedStatesandMexico_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnitedStatesandMexico-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg/220px-Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg/330px-Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg/440px-Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3227" data-file-height="4303" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Capilla_de_San_Francisco_Puebla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Puebla_City" title="Puebla City">Puebla de Zaragoza</a> is the most populated city of <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Afro-Mexican population (1,381,853 individuals as of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-Encuesta_Intercensal_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encuesta_Intercensal-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> is an ethnic group made up of descendants of Colonial-era slaves and recent immigrants of sub-Saharan African descent. Mexico had an active slave trade during the colonial period and some 200,000 Africans were taken there, primarily in the 17th century. The creation of a national Mexican identity, especially after the Mexican Revolution, emphasized Mexico\'s indigenous and European past; it passively eliminated the African ancestors and contributions. Most of the African-descended population was absorbed into the surrounding Mestizo (mixed European/indigenous) and indigenous populations through unions among the groups. Evidence of this long history of intermarriage with Mestizo and indigenous Mexicans is also expressed in the fact that in the 2015 inter-census, 64.9% (896,829) of Afro-Mexicans also identified as indigenous. It was also reported that 9.3% of Afro-Mexicans speak an indigenous language.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> The states with the highest self-report of Afro-Mexicans were Guerrero (6.5% of the population), Oaxaca (4.95%) and Veracruz (3.28%).<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Afro-Mexican culture is strongest in the communities of the <a href="/wiki/Costa_Chica_of_Oaxaca" class="mw-redirect" title="Costa Chica of Oaxaca">Costa Chica of Oaxaca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Costa_Chica_of_Guerrero" title="Costa Chica of Guerrero">Costa Chica of Guerrero</a>.\n</p><p>During the early 20th century, a substantial number of <a href="/wiki/Arab_Mexicans" title="Arab Mexicans">Arabs</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Arab_Christians" title="Arab Christians">Christians</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> began arriving from the crumbling <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. The largest group were the Lebanese and an estimated 400,000 Mexicans have some <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Mexicans" title="Lebanese Mexicans">Lebanese ancestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> Smaller ethnic groups in Mexico include <a href="/wiki/Asian_Mexicans" title="Asian Mexicans">South and East Asians</a>, present since the colonial era. During the colonial era Asians were termed <i>Chino</i> (regardless of ethnicity), and arrived as merchants, artisans and slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Seijas_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seijas-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> The largest group were Filipinos and some 200,000 Mexicans can trace <a href="/wiki/Filipino_immigration_to_Mexico" title="Filipino immigration to Mexico">Filipino ancestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> Modern Asian immigration began in the late 19th century and at one point in the early 20th century, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_immigration_to_Mexico" title="Chinese immigration to Mexico">Chinese</a> were the second largest immigrant group.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_censuses">Official censuses</span></h4>\n<p>The first census in Mexico (then known as <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">New Spain</a>) that included an ethnic classification was the 1793 census. Also known as the Revillagigedo census. Most of its original datasets have reportedly been lost, thus most of what is known about it nowadays comes from essays and field investigations made by academics who had access to the census data and used it as reference for their works such as Prussian geographer <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a>. According to said works Europeans ranged from 18% to 22% of New Spain\'s population, Mestizos from 21% to 25%, Indians from 51% to 61% and Africans were between 6,000 and 10,000. The total population ranged from 3,799,561 to 6,122,354. It is concluded that the population growth trends of whites and mestizos were even, while the percentage of the indigenous population decreased at a rate of 13%\xe2\x80\x9317% per century mostly due the later having higher mortality rates for living in remote locations and being in constant war with the colonists.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> Anthropologist <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonzalo_Aguirre_Beltr%C3%A1n" class="extiw" title="es:Gonzalo Aguirre Beltr\xc3\xa1n">Gonzalo Aguirre Beltr\xc3\xa1n</a> goes beyond said numbers and splits the Mestizo group into "Euromestizos", "Indomestizos" and "Afromestizos" calculating their numbers at more than one million, 700,000 and 600,000 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Aguirre_Beltr\xc3\xa1n_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aguirre_Beltr\xc3\xa1n-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> Independent-era Mexico eliminated the legal basis of the <a href="/wiki/Castas" class="mw-redirect" title="Castas">Colonial caste system</a> which led to exclusion of racial classification in the censuses to come.\n</p><p>According to Mexico\'s second census ever that considered race, made right after the Mexican revolution in 1921,<sup id="cite_ref-somosprimos.com_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somosprimos.com-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> 59% of Mexico\'s population was Mestizo, 29% was Indigenous and only 9% was European, with Mestizos being the most numerous ethno-racial group in almost all the states.<sup id="cite_ref-somosprimos.com_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somosprimos.com-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> For a long time this census\' results were taken as fact, with extraofficial international publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Factbook</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica">Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica</a> using them as a reference to estimate Mexico\'s racial composition up to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia_Britannica_269-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia_Britannica-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> In recent time nonetheless, Mexican academics have subjected the census\' results to scrutiny, claiming that such a drastic alteration in demographic trends in regards to the 1793 census is not possible and cite, among other statistics the relatively low frequency of marriages between people of different continental ancestries in colonial and early independent Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MexicoRacista1_278-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexicoRacista1-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> Said authors claim that the Mexican society went through a "more cultural than biological mestizaje process" sponsored by the state in its efforts to unify the Mexican population which resulted in the inflation of the percentage of the Mestizo Mexican group at the expense of the identity of the other races that exist in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In recent times the Mexican government has decided to conduct new ethnic surveys and censuses, also widening the criteria to classify the ethnicities who were already considered such as the Indigenous Mexican one, which was previously reserved to people who lived in indigenous communities or spoke an indigenous language. According to these recent surveys, Indigenous peoples amount to 23% of Mexico\'s population (including people who declared to be partially indigenous),<sup id="cite_ref-beta.inegi.org.mx_274-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beta.inegi.org.mx-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> Afro-Mexicans are 2% of Mexico\'s population (including people who declared to be partially African)<sup id="cite_ref-beta.inegi.org.mx_274-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beta.inegi.org.mx-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> and European Mexicans amount to 47% of Mexico\'s population (based on appearance rather than on self-declared of ancestry).<sup id="cite_ref-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017_279-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marzo_DiaIntElimDiscRacial_INACCSS_2017-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conapred.org.mx_280-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conapred.org.mx-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DISC-RACIAL_2011_281-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DISC-RACIAL_2011-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> Less numerous groups in Mexico such as Asians and Middle Easterners are also accounted for. Out of all the ethnic groups that have recently been surveyed, that of Mestizos is notably absent, which may be consequence of the ethnic label\'s fluid and subjective definition, which complicates a precise calculation as well the tendency that Mexicans have to identify people with "static" ethnic labels rather than "fluid" ones.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">Emigration</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emigration_from_Mexico" title="Emigration from Mexico">Emigration from Mexico</a></div>\n<p>In the early 1960s, around 600,000 Mexicans lived abroad, which increased sevenfold by the 1990s to 4.4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Migration_Yearbook_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Migration_Yearbook-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> At the turn of the 21st century, this figure more than doubled to 9.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Migration_Yearbook_301-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Migration_Yearbook-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017, it is estimated that 12.9 million Mexicans live abroad, primarily in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, which concentrates nearly 98% of the expatriate population.<sup id="cite_ref-Migration_Yearbook_301-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Migration_Yearbook-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> Majority of Mexicans have settled in states such as <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, particularly around the metropolitan areas of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_metropolitan_area" title="Chicago metropolitan area">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston" title="Greater Houston">Houston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas\xe2\x80\x93Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas-Forth Worth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> As a result of these major migration flows in recent decades, around 36 million U.S. residents, or 11.2% of the country\'s population, identified as being of full or partial Mexican ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> The remaining 2% of expatriates have settled in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (86,000), primarily in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> (49,000) and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (18,000), both European destinations represent almost two-thirds of the Mexican population living in the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-Migration_Yearbook_301-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Migration_Yearbook-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> As for Latin America, it is estimated that 69,000 Mexicans live in the region, <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> (18,000) being the top destination for expatriates, followed by <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> (10,000) and <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> (5,000).<sup id="cite_ref-Migration_Yearbook_301-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Migration_Yearbook-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Mexico" title="Languages of Mexico">Languages of Mexico</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> is the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> national language spoken by the vast majority of the population, making Mexico the world\'s most populous <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">Hispanophone</a> country.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spanishhistory_249-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spanishhistory-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Spanish" title="Mexican Spanish">Mexican Spanish</a> is the set of <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">varieties</a> of the language spoken in the country, which differs from one region to another phonetically, syntactically and lexically.<sup id="cite_ref-Concise_Encyclopedia_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concise_Encyclopedia-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> In general, Mexican Spanish does not make any phonetic <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_Spanish_coronal_fricatives#Seseo" title="Phonological history of Spanish coronal fricatives">distinction among the letters <i>s</i> and <i>z</i></a>, as well as <i>c</i> when preceding the vowels <i>e</i> and <i>i</i>, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Spanish" title="Peninsular Spanish">Peninsular Spanish</a>. The letters <i>b</i> and <i>v</i> have the same pronunciation as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Concise_Encyclopedia_306-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concise_Encyclopedia-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, the usage of <i><a href="/wiki/Voseo" title="Voseo">vos</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">second person</a> <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">singular</a> <a href="/wiki/Pronoun" title="Pronoun">pronoun</a>, found in several Latin American varieties, is replaced by <i><a href="/wiki/T-V_distinction#Spanish" class="mw-redirect" title="T-V distinction">t\xc3\xba</a></i>; whereas <i><a href="/wiki/Spanish_personal_pronouns#The_use_of_vosotros" title="Spanish personal pronouns">vosotros</a></i>, the second person plural pronoun, fell out of use and was effectively replaced by <i>ustedes</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Concise_Encyclopedia_306-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concise_Encyclopedia-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> In written form, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Royal_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Royal Academy">Spanish Royal Academy</a> serves as the primary guideline for spelling, except for words of Amerindian origin that retain their original phonology such as <i><a href="/wiki/Northern_mockingbird" title="Northern mockingbird">cenzontle</a></i> instead of <i>sinzontle</i> and <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Mexico" title="Name of Mexico"><i>M\xc3\xa9xico</i> not <i>M\xc3\xa9jico</i></a>. Words of foreign origin also maintain their original spelling such as whisky and film, as opposed to <i>g\xc3\xbcisqui</i> and <i>filme</i> as the Royal Academy suggests.<sup id="cite_ref-Concise_Encyclopedia_306-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concise_Encyclopedia-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> The letter <i>x</i> is distinctly used in Mexican Spanish, which may be pronounced as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[ks]</span> (as in <i>ox\xc3\xadgeno</i> or <i>taxi</i>), as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xca\x83]</span> particularly in Amerindian words (e.g. <i>mixiote</i>, <i>Xola</i> and <i>uxmal</i>) and as the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">voiceless velar fricative</a> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">x</a>]</span> (such as <i>Texas</i> and <i>Oaxaca</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Concise_Encyclopedia_306-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concise_Encyclopedia-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The federal government officially recognizes <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Mexico#Indigenous_languages" title="Languages of Mexico">sixty-eight linguistic groups and 364 varieties of indigenous languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> It is estimated that around 8.3 million citizens speak these languages,<sup id="cite_ref-Indigenous_Languages_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indigenous_Languages-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a> being the most widely spoken by more than 1.7 million, followed by <a href="/wiki/Yucatec_Maya_language" title="Yucatec Maya language">Yucatec Maya</a> used daily by nearly 850,000 people, <a href="/wiki/Tzeltal_language" title="Tzeltal language">Tzeltal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tzotzil_language" title="Tzotzil language">Tzotzil</a>, two variants of the <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">Mayan languages</a>, are spoken by around half a million people each, primarily in the southern state of <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Indigenous_Languages_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indigenous_Languages-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mixtec_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixtec languages">Mixtec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_languages" title="Zapotec languages">Zapotec</a>, both with estimated 500,000 native speakers each, are two other notorious language groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Indigenous_Languages_308-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indigenous_Languages-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Since its creation in March 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Lenguas_Ind%C3%ADgenas" title="Instituto Nacional de Lenguas Ind\xc3\xadgenas">National Indigenous Languages Institute</a> has been in charge of promoting and protecting the use of the country\'s indigenous languages, through the <a href="/wiki/Ley_General_de_Derechos_Ling%C3%BC%C3%ADsticos_de_los_Pueblos_Ind%C3%ADgenas" title="Ley General de Derechos Ling\xc3\xbc\xc3\xadsticos de los Pueblos Ind\xc3\xadgenas">General Law of Indigenous Peoples\' Linguistic Rights</a>, which recognizes them <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> as "national languages" with equal status as that of Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> Notwithstanding, in practice, indigenous peoples often face discrimination and are unable to have proper access to public services such as education and healthcare, as well as the justice system, as Spanish is the prominent language.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aside from indigenous languages, there are several minority languages spoken in Mexico due to international migration such as <a href="/wiki/Low_German" title="Low German">Low German</a> by the 80,000-strong <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Mexico" title="Mennonites in Mexico">Menonite population</a>, primarily settled in the northern states, fuelled by the tolerance of the federal government towards this community by allowing them to set their own educational system compatible with their customs and traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chipilo_Venetian_dialect" title="Chipilo Venetian dialect">Chipilo dialect</a>, a variance of the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian language</a>, is spoken in the town of <a href="/wiki/Chipilo" title="Chipilo">Chipilo</a>, located in the central state of <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>, by around 2,500 people, mainly descendants of Venetians that migrated to the area in the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is the most commonly taught <a href="/wiki/Foreign_language" title="Foreign language">foreign language</a> in Mexico. It is estimated that nearly 24 million, or around a fifth of the population, study the language through public schools, private institutions or self-access channels.<sup id="cite_ref-313"
