class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> However, a high level of English proficiency is limited to only 5% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is the second most widely taught foreign language, as every year between 200,000 and 250,000 Mexican students enroll in language courses.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_areas">Urban areas</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas_of_Mexico" title="Metropolitan areas of Mexico">Metropolitan areas of id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mexico" title="Religion in Mexico">Religion in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">10%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other Religion</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:green; width:0.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">No religion</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:black; width:5%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">5%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Unspecified</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:gray; width:3%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The 2010 census by the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Estad%C3%ADstica_y_Geograf%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Instituto Nacional de Estad\xc3\xadstica y Geograf\xc3\xada">Instituto Nacional de Estad\xc3\xadstica y Geograf\xc3\xada</a> (National Institute of Statistics and Geography) gave <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Mexico">Roman Catholicism</a> as the main religion, with 83% of the population, while 10% (10,924,103) belong to other Christian denominations, including <a href="/wiki/Evangelicals" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelicals">Evangelicals</a> (5%); <a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> (1.6%); other Protestant or Reformed (0.7%); <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> (1.4%); <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventists</a> (0.6%); and members of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (0.3%).<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> 172,891 (or less than 0.2% of the total) belonged to other, non-Christian religions; 4.7% declared having <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Mexico" title="Irreligion in Mexico">no religion</a>; 2.7% were unspecified.<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg/180px-Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg" width="180" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg/270px-Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg/360px-Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="788" data-file-height="1226" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgen_de_guadalupe1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Our Lady of Guadalupe">Our Lady of Guadalupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of Mexico. This painting of her at the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe">Basilica of Guadalupe</a> is among her most notable depictions; scientists still debate if it should be dated 1531, the year of the first apparition,<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> or the 1550s.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The 92,924,489<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Catholics of Mexico constitute in absolute terms the second largest Catholic community in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>\'s.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> 47% percent of them attend church services weekly.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> The feast day of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Our Lady of Guadalupe">Our Lady of Guadalupe</a>, the patron saint of Mexico, is celebrated on December 12 and is regarded by many Mexicans as the most important religious holiday of their country.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> In spite of this, the Mexican State is officially lay secularist since the separation between religious institutions and the political administration of the nation was enshrined in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Constitution_of_the_United_Mexican_States_of_1857" title="Federal Constitution of the United Mexican States of 1857">1857</a>, and was ratified in the current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico" title="Constitution of Mexico">Constitution of 1917</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Morelos" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Morelos">Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Morelos</a> noted in his writings that there should be no tolerance for any other religion and the <a href="/wiki/1824_Constitution_of_Mexico" title="1824 Constitution of Mexico">Constitution of 1824</a> declared that the official religion of the Republic would be Catholic, and from the second half of 20th century, began a process of introducing creeds different from the Catholic.\n</p><p>The 1920s was marked by a religious conflict known as the <a href="/wiki/Cristero_War" title="Cristero War">Cristero War</a>, in which many peasants encouraged by the clergy clashed with the federal government that had decided to enforce the constitutional laws of 1917. Among the measures contemplated by the Magna Carta were the suppression of the <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">monastic orders</a> and the cancellation of all religious worship. The war ended with an agreement between the parties in conflict (<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> and State), by means of which the respective fields of action were defined. Until the middle of the 1990s, the Mexican constitution did not recognize the existence of any religious group. In 1993, a law was enacted whereby the State granted them legal status as "religious associations". This fact allowed the reestablishment of diplomatic relations with the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>, to which the Mexican State did not recognize as a political entity.\n</p><p>According to the figures of <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_and_Geography_(Mexico)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Institute of Statistics and Geography (Mexico)">INEGI</a>, most Mexicans declare themselves <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> and most <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a> (almost 93 million adherents according to the census of 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\nThe second Christian group is the <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a>, which totals more than 1&#160;million adherents, making the Mexican congregation of this Christian branch the second worldwide.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Thirdly find <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a>, whose members are known as <a href="/wiki/Latter_Day_Saint_movement" title="Latter Day Saint movement">Mormons</a>, 2010 census reported 314,932 members of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints,<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> though the church in 2009 claimed to have over one million registered members;<sup id="cite_ref-lds-Mexico_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lds-Mexico-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/La_Luz_del_Mundo" title="La Luz del Mundo">Church of the La Luz del Mundo</a>, which has its center in "<a href="/w/index.php?title=La_Hermosa_Provincia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="La Hermosa Provincia (page does not exist)">La Hermosa Provincia</a>", a colony of <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a>. The denominations <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal</a> also have an important presence, especially in the cities of the border and in the indigenous communities. In fact, Pentecostal churches together have more than 1.3 million adherents, which in net numbers place them as the second Christian creed in Mexico. The situation changes when the different Pentecostal denominations are considered as separate entities. Other groups are growing, such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iglesia_apost%C3%B3lica_de_la_Fe_en_Cristo_Jes%C3%BAs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Iglesia apost\xc3\xb3lica de la Fe en Cristo Jes\xc3\xbas (page does not exist)">Iglesia apost\xc3\xb3lica de la Fe en Cristo Jes\xc3\xbas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Mexico" title="Mennonites in Mexico">Mennonites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a>. Migratory phenomena have led to the proliferation of different aspects of Christianity, including branches <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholic Churches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>.\n</p><p>According to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacobo_Grinberg-Zylberbaum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jacobo Grinberg-Zylberbaum (page does not exist)">Jacobo Grinberg-Zylberbaum</a> (in texts edited by the <a href="/wiki/National_Autonomous_University_of_Mexico" title="National Autonomous University of Mexico">National Autonomous University of Mexico</a>), it is remarkable the survival of magic-religious rituals of the old <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenouss</a> groups, not only in the current indigenous people but in the <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">whites</a> that make up the Mexican rural and urban society. There is often a <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretism</a> between <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">shamanism</a> and the Catholic tradition. Another religion of popular syncretism in Mexico (especially in recent years) is the <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santer\xc3\xada">Santer\xc3\xada</a>. This is mainly due to the large number of Cubans who settled in the territory after the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> (mainly in states such as <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Yucat\xc3\xa1n</a>). Although Mexico was also a recipient of black slaves from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> in the 16th century, the apogee of these cults is relatively new.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In certain regions, the profession of a creed other than the Catholic is seen as a threat to community unity. It is argued that the Catholic religion is part of the ethnic identity, and that the Protestants are not willing to participate in the traditional customs and practices (the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tequio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tequio (page does not exist)">tequio</a> or community work, participation in the festivities and similar issues). The refusal of the Protestants is because their religious beliefs do not allow them to participate in the cult of images. In extreme cases, tension between Catholics and Protestants has led to the expulsion or even murder of Protestants in several villages. The best known cases are those of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Chamula" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Chamula">San Juan Chamula</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> in Chiapas, and San Nicol\xc3\xa1s, in <a href="/wiki/Ixmiquilpan" title="Ixmiquilpan">Ixmiquilpan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(state)" title="Hidalgo (state)">Hidalgo</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG/200px-D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG/300px-D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG/400px-D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3472" data-file-height="2604" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%ADa_de_muertos_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Offering of <a href="/wiki/Day_of_the_Dead" title="Day of the Dead">Day of the Dead</a> (<i>D\xc3\xada de Muertos</i>).</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg/200px-The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg/300px-The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg/400px-The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Kid_-_Diego_Rivera.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Detail of the 1947 mural of <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a> that created <a href="/wiki/La_Calavera_Catrina" title="La Calavera Catrina">La Catrina</a>. The image of La  Catrina is commonly seen reflected as part of the Day of the Dead (<i>D\xc3\xada de Muertos</i>) celebrations throughout the country.</div></div></div>\n<p>A similar argument was presented by a committee of anthropologists to request the government of the Republic to expel the <a href="/wiki/SIL_International" title="SIL International">Summer Linguistic Institute</a> (SIL), in the year 1979, which was accused of promoting the division of indigenous peoples by translating the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> into vernacular languages and evangelizing in a Protestant creed that threatened the integrity of popular cultures. The Mexican government paid attention to the call of the anthropologists and canceled the agreement that had held with the SIL. Conflicts have also occurred in other areas of social life. For example, given that Jehovah\'s Witnesses are prohibited from surrendering honors to national symbols (something that is done every Monday in Mexican public schools), children who have been educated in that religion were expelled from public schools. This type of problem can only be solved with the intervention of the National Commission of <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Rights">Human Rights</a>, and not always with favorable results for children.\n</p><p>The impact of the Catholic religion in Mexico has also caused a fusion of elements. Beyond churches and religious denominations, a phenomenon persists in Mexico that some anthropologists and sociologists call "popular religion", that is, religion as the practice and understanding of the people. In Mexico, the main component is the Catholic religion, to which elements of other beliefs have been added, already of pre-Hispanic, African or Asian origin. In general, popular religiosity is viewed with bad eyes by institutionally structured religions. One of the most exemplary cases of popular religiosity is the cult of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Muerte" title="Santa Muerte">Holy Dead</a> (Santa Muerte). The Catholic hierarchy insists on describing it as a satanic cult. However, most of the people who profess this cult declare themselves to be Catholic believers, and consider that there is no contradiction between the tributes they offer to the <i>White Child</i> and the adoration of God. Other examples are the representations of the <a href="/wiki/Stations_of_the_Cross" title="Stations of the Cross">Passion of Christ</a> and the celebration of <a href="/wiki/Day_of_the_Dead" title="Day of the Dead">Day of the Dead</a>, which take place within the framework of the Catholic Christian imaginary, but under a very particular reinterpretation of its protagonists.\n</p><p>The presence of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Mexico" title="History of the Jews in Mexico">Jews in Mexico</a> dates back to 1521, when Hern\xc3\xa1n Cort\xc3\xa9s conquered the Aztecs, accompanied by several <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">Conversos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup>  According to the 2010 census, there are 67,476 Jews in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Mexico" title="Islam in Mexico">Islam in Mexico</a> is practiced mostly by <a href="/wiki/Arab_Mexican" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab Mexican">Arab Mexicans</a>, while there is also a small community of Muslims among indigenous Mexicans around the <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_las_Casas" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de las Casas">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de las Casas</a> area in Chiapas.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> In the 2010 census 18,185 Mexicans reported belonging to an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern religion">Eastern religion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2010-census_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> a category which includes a tiny <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Mexico" title="Buddhism in Mexico">Buddhist</a> population.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Mexico" title="Women in Mexico">Women in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Until the twentieth century, Mexico was an overwhelmingly rural country, with rural women\'s status defined within the context of the family and local community.  With urbanization beginning in the sixteenth century, following the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec empire">Spanish conquest of the Aztec empire</a>, cities have provided economic and social opportunities not possible within rural villages.\n</p><p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Mexico has the 16th highest rate of homicides committed against women in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-femicide_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-femicide-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> A study in 1997 showed that the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a> against women in Mexican marital relationships varies at between 30 and 60 percent of relationships.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> The remains of the victims were frequently mutilated.<sup id="cite_ref-hp_8Jan2015_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hp_8Jan2015-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> According to a 1997 study, domestic abuse in Mexican culture "is embedded in gender and marital relations fostered in Mexican women\'s dependence on their spouses for subsistence and for self-esteem, sustained by ideologies of romantic love, by family structure and residential arrangements".<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> The perpetrators are often the boyfriend, father-in-law, ex-husbands or husbands but only 1.6% of the murder cases led to an arrest and sentencing.<sup id="cite_ref-hp_8Jan2015_334-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hp_8Jan2015-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(September 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Mexico" title="Culture of Mexico">Culture of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG/220px-TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG/330px-TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG/440px-TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TiledBldgs5OrientePuebla.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Talavera_pottery" title="Talavera pottery">Talavera pottery</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Mexican culture reflects the complexity of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mexico" title="History of Mexico">country\'s history</a> through the blending of indigenous cultures and the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Spain" title="Culture of Spain">culture of Spain</a>, imparted during Spain\'s 300-year colonization of Mexico. Exogenous cultural elements have been incorporated into Mexican culture as time has passed.\n</p><p>The Porfirian era (<i>el <a href="/wiki/Porfirio_D%C3%ADaz" title="Porfirio D\xc3\xadaz">Porfiriato</a></i>), in the last quarter of the 19th century and the first decade of the 20th century, was marked by economic progress and peace. After four decades of civil unrest and war, Mexico saw the development of philosophy and the arts, promoted by President D\xc3\xadaz himself. Since that time, as accentuated during the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a>, cultural identity has had its foundation in the <i>mestizaje</i>, of which the indigenous (i.e. Amerindian) element is the core. In light of the various ethnicities that formed the Mexican people, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vasconcelos" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos">Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos</a> in his publication <i>La Raza C\xc3\xb3smica</i> (The Cosmic Race) (1925) defined Mexico to be the melting pot of all races (thus extending the definition of the <i>mestizo</i>) not only biologically but culturally as well.<sup id="cite_ref-vasconcelos160_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vasconcelos160-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Painting">Painting</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_art" title="Mexican art">Mexican art</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Kodeks_nuttall3.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kodeks_nuttall3.jpeg/200px-Kodeks_nuttall3.jpeg" width="200" height="145" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kodeks_nuttall3.jpeg/300px-Kodeks_nuttall3.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kodeks_nuttall3.jpeg/400px-Kodeks_nuttall3.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="574" data-file-height="415" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Many <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_codices" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesoamerican codices">codices</a> made both during Pre-hispanic Mexico and in the Spanish colony are preserved.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Lactaci%C3%B3n_de_Santo_Domingo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lactaci%C3%B3n_de_Santo_Domingo.JPG/200px-Lactaci%C3%B3n_de_Santo_Domingo.JPG" width="200" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lactaci%C3%B3n_de_Santo_Domingo.JPG/300px-Lactaci%C3%B3n_de_Santo_Domingo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lactaci%C3%B3n_de_Santo_Domingo.JPG/400px-Lactaci%C3%B3n_de_Santo_Domingo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="875" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The art of the Colonial Mexico (center of New Spain) developed a large number of painters born in Mexico. Now these works are preserved in museums in many cities of Mexico.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Murales_Rivera_-_Ausbeutung_durch_die_Spanier_1_perspective.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Murales_Rivera_-_Ausbeutung_durch_die_Spanier_1_perspective.jpg/200px-Murales_Rivera_-_Ausbeutung_durch_die_Spanier_1_perspective.jpg" width="200" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Murales_Rivera_-_Ausbeutung_durch_die_Spanier_1_perspective.jpg/300px-Murales_Rivera_-_Ausbeutung_durch_die_Spanier_1_perspective.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Murales_Rivera_-_Ausbeutung_durch_die_Spanier_1_perspective.jpg/400px-Murales_Rivera_-_Ausbeutung_durch_die_Spanier_1_perspective.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2684" data-file-height="2384" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Mexican_Muralism" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican Muralism">Mexican Muralism</a>. A cultural expression starting in the 1920s created by a group of intellectual Mexican painters after the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a>, reinforced by the Great Depression and the First World War.<sup id="cite_ref-aguilar_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aguilar-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a> is one of the oldest arts in Mexico. The cave painting in Mexican territory is about 7500 years old, and has been manifested in the caves of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>. Pre-Hispanic Mexico is present in buildings and caves, in <a href="/wiki/Aztec_codices" title="Aztec codices">Aztec codices</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Ceramics" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceramics">ceramics</a>, in garments, etc. .; examples of this are the <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a> mural paintings of <a href="/wiki/Bonampak" title="Bonampak">Bonampak</a>, or those of <a href="/wiki/Teotihuac%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Teotihuac\xc3\xa1n">Teotihuac\xc3\xa1n</a>, those of <a href="/wiki/Cacaxtla" title="Cacaxtla">Cacaxtla</a> and those of <a href="/wiki/Monte_Alb%C3%A1n" title="Monte Alb\xc3\xa1n">Monte Alb\xc3\xa1n</a>.\n</p><p>The mural painting had an important flowering during the 16th century, the same in religious constructions as in houses of lineage; such is the case of the convents of <a href="/wiki/Acolman" title="Acolman">Acolman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Actopan,_Hidalgo" title="Actopan, Hidalgo">Actopan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huejotzingo" title="Huejotzingo">Huejotzingo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tecamachalco,_Puebla" title="Tecamachalco, Puebla">Tecamachalco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zinacantepec" class="mw-redirect" title="Zinacantepec">Zinacantepec</a>. It is said that they were mainly indigenous painters led by friars who made them. These were also manifested in illustrated manuscripts such as the <a href="/wiki/Matr%C3%ADcula_de_Tributos" title="Matr\xc3\xadcula de Tributos">Matr\xc3\xadcula de Tributos</a>.\n</p><p>For a time it was believed that the first European painter living in <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rodrigo_de_Cifuentes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rodrigo de Cifuentes (page does not exist)">Rodrigo de Cifuentes</a>, an apocryphal artist who even came to be attributed works such as <i>The Baptism of the <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">Caciques</a> de Tlaxcala</i>, painting of the main altarpiece of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Convento_de_San_Francisco,_Tlaxcala&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Convento de San Francisco, Tlaxcala (page does not exist)">Convent of San Francisco</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tlaxcala" title="Tlaxcala">Tlaxcala</a>. Among the native painters was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marcos_Aquino&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marcos Aquino (page does not exist)">Marcos Aquino</a>. The religiosity of the Novohispanos ("New-spanish") made that the painting was important for the evangelization of the society, the friars realized the graphic skills of the natives, who enriched the baroque and <a href="/wiki/Mannerist" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannerist">mannerist</a> style. The arrival of several European painters and some students from New Spain, such as <a href="/wiki/Juan_Correa" title="Juan Correa">Juan Correa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crist%C3%B3bal_de_Villalpando" title="Crist\xc3\xb3bal de Villalpando">Crist\xc3\xb3bal de Villalpando</a> or <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cabrera_(painter)" title="Miguel Cabrera (painter)">Miguel Cabrera</a>, who made the walls and altarpieces the main source of ideological and political expression of artists.\n</p><p>The painting of the 19th century had a very marked romantic influence, landscapes and portraits were the greatest expression of this era. <a href="/wiki/Hermenegildo_Bustos" title="Hermenegildo Bustos">Hermenegildo Bustos</a> is one of the most appreciated painters of the <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">historiography</a> of Mexican art. They also emphasize in these years <a href="/w/index.php?title=Santiago_Rebull&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Santiago Rebull (page does not exist)">Santiago Rebull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Salom%C3%A9_Pina" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Salom\xc3\xa9 Pina">Jos\xc3\xa9 Salom\xc3\xa9 Pina</a>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Parra" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Parra">F\xc3\xa9lix Parra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Landesio" title="Eugenio Landesio">Eugenio Landesio</a> and his famous disciple, the landscaper <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Velasco_G%C3%B3mez" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Velasco G\xc3\xb3mez">Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Velasco G\xc3\xb3mez</a>, as well like <a href="/wiki/Julio_Ruelas" title="Julio Ruelas">Julio Ruelas</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mexican_art" title="Mexican art">Mexican painting</a> of the 20th century has achieved world renown with figures such as <a href="/wiki/David_Alfaro_Siqueiros" title="David Alfaro Siqueiros">David Alfaro Siqueiros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Clemente_Orozco" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Clemente Orozco">Jos\xc3\xa9 Clemente Orozco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Clausell" title="Joaqu\xc3\xadn Clausell">Joaqu\xc3\xadn Clausell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frida_Kahlo" title="Frida Kahlo">Frida Kahlo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a>, generation of idealists who marked the image of modern Mexico in the face of strong social and economic criticism. The Oaxacan School quickly gained fame and prestige, diffusion of an ancestral and modern culture, freedom of design is observed in relation to the color and texture of the canvases and murals as a period of transition between the 20th century and the 21st century.\n</p><p>Some of the most outstanding painters in the 21st century (current painters): <a href="/w/index.php?title=Patricia_Calvo_Guzm%C3%A1n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Patricia Calvo Guzm\xc3\xa1n (page does not exist)">Patricia Calvo Guzm\xc3\xa1n</a>. She studied painting in Beijing. Her work, of marked oriental influence, recalls the cut paper figures of Mexico and China, mixing them with a rich chromatic range; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eliseo_Garza_Aguilar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eliseo Garza Aguilar (page does not exist)">Eliseo Garza Aguilar</a>, painter and <a href="/wiki/Performer" class="mw-redirect" title="Performer">performer</a> considered among the leading exponents of the provocative and reflective art of the Third Millennium; in search of a critical response from the spectators, he combines his pictorial work in the <a href="/wiki/Performance" title="Performance">performances</a> with theatrical histrionics; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilar_Goutas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pilar Goutas (page does not exist)">Pilar Goutas</a>, a painter who uses oil on amate support, with strong influence from <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Pollock" title="Jackson Pollock">Jackson Pollock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_calligraphy" title="Chinese calligraphy">Chinese calligraphy</a>; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rafael_Torres_Correa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rafael Torres Correa (page does not exist)">Rafael Torres Correa</a> settles his residence in Mexico in 2001 and joins the contemporary art workshop "La Polilla" in <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a>, and performs various plastic and scenographic projects.\n</p><p>Throughout history several prominent painters of different nationalities have expressed in their works the face of Mexico. Among the most outstanding we can mention <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Thomas_Egerton" title="Daniel Thomas Egerton">Daniel Thomas Egerton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Nebel" title="Carl Nebel">Carl Nebel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Moran" title="Thomas Moran">Thomas Moran</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard_Manet" title="\xc3\x89douard Manet">\xc3\x89douard Manet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonora_Carrington" title="Leonora Carrington">Leonora Carrington</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sculpture">Sculpture</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sculpture_in_Mexico" title="Sculpture in Mexico">Sculpture in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>Sculpture in Mexico is strongly manifested in Mesoamerican pre-Columbian cultures (<a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Mayans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olmec" class="mw-redirect" title="Olmec">Olmecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">Toltecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mixtec" title="Mixtec">Mixtecs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aztec" class="mw-redirect" title="Aztec">Aztecs</a>), etc., being this generally religious.\n</p><p>From the Spanish conquest, civil and religious sculpture is worked by indigenous artists, with guidance from teachers of the peninsula, so some pre-Hispanic features are shown. Since the 17th century, white and <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> sculptors have created works with a marked influence of European classicism.\n</p><p>Romanticism tended to break the strict norms and models of classicism, as it pursued ideas influenced by realism and nationalism. The religious sculpture was reduced to a sporadic imagery, while the secular sculpture continued in portraits and monumental art of a civic nature. Between 1820 and 1880 the predominant themes were, successively: religious images, biblical scenes, allegories to the symbols of the insurgency movement and scenes and characters of pre-Cortesian history, and portraits of the old aristocracy, of the nascent bourgeoisie and commanders of the pre-revolution. The transcendent was to introduce civil reasons, the first national types and glimpses of a current of self-expression.\n</p><p>During the 20th century, great exponents of Mexican sculpture are <a href="/wiki/Juan_Soriano" title="Juan Soriano">Juan Soriano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Cuevas" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Cuevas">Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Cuevas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_(sculptor)" title="Sebasti\xc3\xa1n (sculptor)">Enrique Carbajal</a> (<i>Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</i>), English <a href="/wiki/Leonora_Carrington" title="Leonora Carrington">Leonora Carrington</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Mexico" title="Architecture of Mexico">Architecture of Mexico</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:SSA41434.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/SSA41434.JPG/200px-SSA41434.JPG" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/SSA41434.JPG/300px-SSA41434.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/SSA41434.JPG/400px-SSA41434.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Teotihuac%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Teotihuac\xc3\xa1n">Teotihuac\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_cortez_9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Palacio_de_cortez_9.jpg/200px-Palacio_de_cortez_9.jpg" width="200" height="151" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Palacio_de_cortez_9.jpg/300px-Palacio_de_cortez_9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Palacio_de_cortez_9.jpg/400px-Palacio_de_cortez_9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="816" data-file-height="616" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Cort%C3%A9s,_Cuernavaca" title="Palace of Cort\xc3\xa9s, Cuernavaca">Palace of Cort\xc3\xa9s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a>, is the oldest conserved colonial-era civil structure in the continental Americas.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_zacatecas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Catedral_zacatecas.jpg/200px-Catedral_zacatecas.jpg" width="200" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Catedral_zacatecas.jpg/300px-Catedral_zacatecas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Catedral_zacatecas.jpg/400px-Catedral_zacatecas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1054" data-file-height="770" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Zacatecas_Cathedral" title="Zacatecas Cathedral">Zacatecas Cathedral</a></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The presence of the human being in the Mexican territory has left important archaeological findings of great importance for the explanation of the habitat of primitive man and contemporary man. The Mesoamerican civilizations managed to have great stylistic development and proportion on the human and urban scale, the form was evolving from simplicity to aesthetic complexity; in the north of the country the adobe and stone architecture is manifested, the multifamily housing as we can see in <a href="/wiki/Casas_Grandes" title="Casas Grandes">Casas Grandes</a>; and the troglodyte dwelling in caves of the Sierra Madre Occidental.\n</p><p>Urbanism had a great development in pre-Hispanic cultures, where we can see the magnitude of the cities of <a href="/wiki/Teotihuac%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Teotihuac\xc3\xa1n">Teotihuac\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tula_(Mesoamerican_site)" title="Tula (Mesoamerican site)">Tollan-Xicocotitlan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">M\xc3\xa9xico-Tenochtitlan</a>, within the environmentalist urbanism highlight the Mayan cities to be incorporated into the monumentality of its buildings with the thickness of the jungle and complex networks of roads called <i>sakb\xc3\xa9s</i>.\n</p><p>With the arrival of the Spaniards, architectural theories of the Greco-Roman order with Arab influences were introduced. Due to the process of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Evangelization_in_New_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Evangelization in New Spain (page does not exist)">evangelization</a>, when the first monastic temples and monasteries were built, their own models were projected, such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mendicant_monasteries_in_Mexico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mendicant monasteries in Mexico (page does not exist)">mendicant monasteries</a>, unique in their type in architecture. The interaction between Spaniards and natives gave rise to artistic styles such as the so-called <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tequitqui&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tequitqui (page does not exist)">tequitqui</a></i> (from <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a>: worker). Years later the baroque and mannerism were imposed in large cathedrals and civil buildings, while rural areas are built <a href="/wiki/Hacienda" title="Hacienda">haciendas</a> or stately farms with Mozarabic tendencies.\n</p><p>In the 19th century the neoclassical movement arose as a response to the objectives of the republican nation, one of its examples are the <a href="/wiki/Hospicio_Caba%C3%B1as" title="Hospicio Caba\xc3\xb1as">Hospicio Caba\xc3\xb1as</a> where the strict plastic of the classical orders are represented in their architectural elements, new religious buildings also arise, civilian and military that demonstrate the presence of neoclassicism. Romanticists from a past seen through archeology show images of medieval Europe, Islamic and pre-Hispanic Mexico in the form of architectural elements in the construction of international exhibition pavilions looking for an identity typical of the national culture. The <i>art nouveau</i>, and the <i>art deco</i> were styles introduced into the design of the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a> to mark the identity of the Mexican nation with Greek-Roman and pre-Hispanic symbols.\n</p><p>Modern architecture in Mexico has an important development in the plasticity of form and space, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Villagr%C3%A1n_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Villagr\xc3\xa1n Garc\xc3\xada">Jos\xc3\xa9 Villagr\xc3\xa1n Garc\xc3\xada</a> develops a theory of form that sets the pattern of teaching in many schools of architecture in the country within functionalism. The emergence of the new <a href="/wiki/Mexican_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican architecture">Mexican architecture</a> was born as a formal order of the policies of a nationalist state that sought modernity and the differentiation of other nations. <a href="/wiki/Juan_O%27Gorman" title="Juan O&#39;Gorman">Juan O\'Gorman</a> was one of the first environmental architects in Mexico, developing the "organic" theory, trying to integrate the building with the landscape within the same approaches of <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright" title="Frank Lloyd Wright">Frank Lloyd Wright</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> In the search for a new architecture that does not resemble the styles of the past, it achieves a joint manifestation with the mural painting and the <a href="/wiki/Landscaping" title="Landscaping">landscaping</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jalisco_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jalisco School (page does not exist)">Jalisco School</a> was a proposal of those socio-political movements that the country demanded. <a href="/wiki/Luis_Barrag%C3%A1n" title="Luis Barrag\xc3\xa1n">Luis Barrag\xc3\xa1n</a> managed to combine the shape of the space with forms of rural vernacular architecture of Mexico and Mediterranean countries (Spain-Morocco), integrating an impressive color that handles light and shade in different tones and opens a look at the international <a href="/wiki/Minimalism" title="Minimalism">minimalism</a>.\n</p><p>Mexican architecture is a cultural phenomenon born of the ideology of nationalist governments of the 20th century, which was shaping the identity image by its colorful and variegated ornamental elements inherited from ancestral cultures, classical and monumental forms and, subsequently, the incorporation of modernism and cutting-edge international trends.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="The_Mexican_.28Lo_mexicano.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Mexican_(Lo_mexicano)">The Mexican (Lo mexicano)</span></h3>\n<p>In ethnic and cultural terms, <i>Lo mexicano</i> corresponds only to everything that is referred to the <a href="/wiki/Aztec" class="mw-redirect" title="Aztec">Aztec</a> culture; therefore, ethnically Mexicans are those who are also known as <i><a href="/wiki/Nahua_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahua peoples">Nahuas</a></i> and whose language is <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> There is a strong discussion to define The Mexican (Lo mexicano); There are two completely divided aspects: ethnic and cultural, which focuses exclusively on the <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerican</a> people called <i>Mexica people</i>, and the legal-administrative aspect of the territory called <i>Mexico</i>. In legal terms and in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico" title="Constitution of Mexico">Constitution</a>, <i>Mexican</i> is a citizen born within the territory of the United Mexican States or whoever has decided adopt the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_citizenship" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican citizenship">Mexican citizenship</a>.\n</p><p><i>The Mexican</i> could be what characterizes the being of Mexico and its people; however, it is an ethnic concept that only defines the mestizo identity that had been related for a long time and that is limited with respect to the ethnic diversity of the country. It is an intellectual construction product of the approaches of specialists to the <a href="/wiki/Cultural" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural">cultural</a> reality of the country. In trying to capture in a single figure the <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multicultural</a> reality of Mexico, the result of the intellectual analysis has produced a series of <a href="/wiki/Stereotype" title="Stereotype">stereotypes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Truism" title="Truism">truisms</a> about what it is to be a Mexican. This discourse about The Mexican has been used in the political field to legitimize power, and at the same time it is imposed on the population of the country as a fact beyond all doubt.\n</p><p>The intellectual construction of the <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> is in dialogue with the triumph of revolutionary nationalism, which was born after the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a>. In the reflection on the subject (the character of the Mexican, the mexicanity, the definition of a Mexican) have participated, among others: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vasconcelos_Calder%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos Calder\xc3\xb3n">Jos\xc3\xa9 Vasconcelos</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Ramos" title="Samuel Ramos">Samuel Ramos</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Uranga" title="Emilio Uranga">Emilio Uranga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gaos" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Gaos">Jos\xc3\xa9 Gaos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Zea_Aguilar" title="Leopoldo Zea Aguilar">Leopoldo Zea</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jorge_Portilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jorge Portilla (page does not exist)">Jorge Portilla</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Santiago_Ram%C3%ADrez_Sandoval&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Santiago Ram\xc3\xadrez Sandoval (page does not exist)">Santiago Ram\xc3\xadrez</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Salvador_P%C3%A9rez_Nevares&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Salvador P\xc3\xa9rez Nevares (page does not exist)">Salvador P\xc3\xa9rez Nevares</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Bartra" title="Roger Bartra">Roger Bartra</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_del_Val&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 del Val (page does not exist)">Jos\xc3\xa9 del Val</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Warman" title="Arturo Warman">Arturo Warman</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aniceto_Aramoni&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aniceto Aramoni (page does not exist)">Aniceto Aramoni</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rogelio_D%C3%ADaz_Guerrero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rogelio D\xc3\xadaz Guerrero (page does not exist)">Rogelio D\xc3\xadaz Guerrero</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ezequiel_Adeodato_Ch%C3%A1vez_Lavista&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ezequiel Adeodato Ch\xc3\xa1vez Lavista (page does not exist)">Ezequiel Adeodato Ch\xc3\xa1vez Lavista</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauro_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Estrada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mauro Rodr\xc3\xadguez Estrada (page does not exist)">Mauro Rodr\xc3\xadguez Estrada</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carlos_Chilpa_Navarrete&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carlos Chilpa Navarrete (page does not exist)">Carlos Chilpa Navarrete</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> In this specific topic, occupies a privileged place <a href="/wiki/Octavio_Paz" title="Octavio Paz">Octavio Paz</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Labyrinth_of_Solitude" title="The Labyrinth of Solitude">The Labyrinth of Solitude</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_literature" title="Mexican literature">Mexican literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_literature" title="Mesoamerican literature">Mesoamerican literature</a></div>\n<p>Mexican literature has its antecedents in the literatures of the indigenous settlements of Mesoamerica. The most well known prehispanic poet is <a href="/wiki/Nezahualcoyotl_(tlatoani)" title="Nezahualcoyotl (tlatoani)">Nezahualcoyotl</a>. Modern Mexican literature was influenced by the concepts of the Spanish colonialization of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>. Outstanding colonial writers and poets include <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ruiz_de_Alarc%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ruiz de Alarc\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ruiz de Alarc\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juana_In%C3%A9s_de_la_Cruz" title="Juana In\xc3\xa9s de la Cruz">Juana In\xc3\xa9s de la Cruz</a>.\n</p><p>Other writers include <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Reyes" title="Alfonso Reyes">Alfonso Reyes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Lizardi" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Joaqu\xc3\xadn Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lizardi">Jos\xc3\xa9 Joaqu\xc3\xadn Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lizardi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Manuel_Altamirano" title="Ignacio Manuel Altamirano">Ignacio Manuel Altamirano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Fuentes" title="Carlos Fuentes">Carlos Fuentes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Octavio_Paz" title="Octavio Paz">Octavio Paz</a> (Nobel Laureate), <a href="/wiki/Renato_Leduc" title="Renato Leduc">Renato Leduc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Monsiv%C3%A1is" title="Carlos Monsiv\xc3\xa1is">Carlos Monsiv\xc3\xa1is</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elena_Poniatowska" title="Elena Poniatowska">Elena Poniatowska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Azuela" title="Mariano Azuela">Mariano Azuela</a> ("Los de abajo") and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rulfo" title="Juan Rulfo">Juan Rulfo</a> ("Pedro P\xc3\xa1ramo"). <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Traven" class="mw-redirect" title="Bruno Traven">Bruno Traven</a> wrote "Canasta de cuentos mexicanos" (Mexican tales basket), "El tesoro de la Sierra Madre" (Treasure of the Sierra Madre).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_art" title="Mexican art">Mexican art</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg/250px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg/375px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg/500px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9028.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a> is the preeminent fine arts hall in Mexico.</div></div></div>\n<p>Post-revolutionary art in Mexico had its expression in the works of renowned artists such as <a href="/wiki/David_Alfaro_Siqueiros" title="David Alfaro Siqueiros">David Alfaro Siqueiros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federico_Cant%C3%BA_Garza" title="Federico Cant\xc3\xba Garza">Federico Cant\xc3\xba Garza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frida_Kahlo" title="Frida Kahlo">Frida Kahlo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_O%27Gorman" title="Juan O&#39;Gorman">Juan O\'Gorman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Clemente_Orozco" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Clemente Orozco">Jos\xc3\xa9 Clemente Orozco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rufino_Tamayo" title="Rufino Tamayo">Rufino Tamayo</a>. Diego Rivera, the most well-known figure of Mexican muralism, painted the <a href="/wiki/Man_at_the_Crossroads" title="Man at the Crossroads">Man at the Crossroads</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a> in New York City, a huge mural that was destroyed the next year because of the inclusion of a portrait of Russian communist leader <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Lenin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> Some of Rivera\'s murals are displayed at the Mexican <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Mexico)" title="National Palace (Mexico)">National Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palace of Fine Arts</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_architecture" title="Mesoamerican architecture">Mesoamerican architecture</a> is mostly noted for its pyramids which are the largest such structures outside of Ancient Egypt.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_architecture" title="Spanish Colonial architecture">Spanish Colonial architecture</a> is marked by the contrast between the simple, solid construction demanded by the new environment and the Baroque ornamentation exported from Spain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Mexico, as the center of New Spain has some of the most renowned buildings built in this style.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Mexico" title="Cinema of Mexico">Cinema of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg/170px-Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg/255px-Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="340" data-file-height="453" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Actress <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del R\xc3\xado">Dolores del R\xc3\xado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> star in the 1920s and 1930s and prominent figure of the <i><a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Mexican_cinema" title="Golden Age of Mexican cinema">Golden Age of Mexican cinema</a></i> in the 1940s and 1950s</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Mexico" title="Cinema of Mexico">Mexican films</a> from the <i><a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Mexican_cinema" title="Golden Age of Mexican cinema">Golden Age</a></i> in the 1940s and 1950s are the greatest examples of Latin American cinema, with a huge industry comparable to the Hollywood of those years. Mexican films were exported and exhibited in all of Latin America and Europe. <i><a href="/wiki/Maria_Candelaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Candelaria">Maria Candelaria</a></i> (1943) by <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Emilio Fern\xc3\xa1ndez">Emilio Fern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>, was one of the first films awarded a <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d&#39;Or">Palme d\'Or</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a> in 1946, the first time the event was held after World War II. The famous Spanish-born director <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bu%C3%B1uel" title="Luis Bu\xc3\xb1uel">Luis Bu\xc3\xb1uel</a> realized in Mexico between 1947 and 1965 some of his masterpieces like <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Olvidados" title="Los Olvidados">Los Olvidados</a></i> (1949) and <i><a href="/wiki/Viridiana" title="Viridiana">Viridiana</a></i> (1961). Famous actors and actresses from this period include <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_F%C3%A9lix" title="Mar\xc3\xada F\xc3\xa9lix">Mar\xc3\xada F\xc3\xa9lix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Infante" title="Pedro Infante">Pedro Infante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del R\xc3\xado">Dolores del R\xc3\xado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Negrete" title="Jorge Negrete">Jorge Negrete</a> and the comedian <a href="/wiki/Cantinflas" title="Cantinflas">Cantinflas</a>.\n</p><p>More recently, films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Like_Water_for_Chocolate_(film)" title="Like Water for Chocolate (film)">Como agua para chocolate</a></i> (1992), <i><a href="/wiki/Cronos_(film)" title="Cronos (film)">Cronos</a></i> (1993), <i><a href="/wiki/Y_tu_mam%C3%A1_tambi%C3%A9n" class="mw-redirect" title="Y tu mam\xc3\xa1 tambi\xc3\xa9n">Y tu mam\xc3\xa1 tambi\xc3\xa9n</a></i> (2001), and <i><a href="/wiki/Pan%27s_Labyrinth" title="Pan&#39;s Labyrinth">Pan\'s Labyrinth</a></i> (2006) have been successful in creating universal stories about contemporary subjects, and were internationally recognized, as in the prestigious Cannes Film Festival. Mexican directors <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Gonz%C3%A1lez_I%C3%B1%C3%A1rritu" title="Alejandro Gonz\xc3\xa1lez I\xc3\xb1\xc3\xa1rritu">Alejandro Gonz\xc3\xa1lez I\xc3\xb1\xc3\xa1rritu</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Amores_perros" title="Amores perros">Amores perros</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Babel_(film)" title="Babel (film)">Babel</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Birdman_(film)" title="Birdman (film)">Birdman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Revenant_(2015_film)" title="The Revenant (2015 film)">The Revenant</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n">Alfonso Cuar\xc3\xb3n</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Children_of_Men" title="Children of Men">Children of Men</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_(2013_film)" title="Gravity (2013 film)">Gravity</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_del_Toro" title="Guillermo del Toro">Guillermo del Toro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Carrera" title="Carlos Carrera">Carlos Carrera</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/El_crimen_del_Padre_Amaro" class="mw-redirect" title="El crimen del Padre Amaro">The Crime of Father Amaro</a></i>), screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Arriaga" title="Guillermo Arriaga">Guillermo Arriaga</a> and photographer <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Lubezki" title="Emmanuel Lubezki">Emmanuel Lubezki</a> are some of the most known present-day film makers.\n</p><p>Some Mexican actors have achieved recognition as Hollywood stars. These include <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Novarro" title="Ramon Novarro">Ramon Novarro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del R\xc3\xado">Dolores del R\xc3\xado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lupe_V%C3%A9lez" title="Lupe V\xc3\xa9lez">Lupe V\xc3\xa9lez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Roland" title="Gilbert Roland">Gilbert Roland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Quinn" title="Anthony Quinn">Anthony Quinn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katy_Jurado" title="Katy Jurado">Katy Jurado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Montalb%C3%A1n" title="Ricardo Montalb\xc3\xa1n">Ricardo Montalb\xc3\xa1n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salma_Hayek" title="Salma Hayek">Salma Hayek</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican television">Mexican television</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Mexico" title="List of newspapers in Mexico">List of newspapers in Mexico</a></div>\n<p>There are three major television companies in Mexico that own the primary networks and broadcast covering all nation, <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/TV_Azteca" title="TV Azteca">TV Azteca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imagen_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Imagen Television">Imagen Television</a>. Televisa is also the largest producer of Spanish-language content in the world and also the world\'s largest Spanish-language media network.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> Media company <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Imagen" title="Grupo Imagen">Grupo Imagen</a> is another national coverage television broadcaster in Mexico, that also owns the newspaper <a href="/wiki/Exc%C3%A9lsior" title="Exc\xc3\xa9lsior">Exc\xc3\xa9lsior</a>. <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Multimedios" title="Grupo Multimedios">Grupo Multimedios</a> is another media conglomerate with Spanish-language broadcasting in Mexico, Spain, and the United States. The <i><a href="/wiki/Telenovela" title="Telenovela">telenovelas</a></i> are very traditional in Mexico and are translated to many languages and seen all over the world with renowned names like <a href="/wiki/Ver%C3%B3nica_Castro" title="Ver\xc3\xb3nica Castro">Ver\xc3\xb3nica Castro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A9ndez" title="Luc\xc3\xada M\xc3\xa9ndez">Luc\xc3\xada M\xc3\xa9ndez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thal%C3%ADa" title="Thal\xc3\xada">Thal\xc3\xada</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mexico" title="Music of Mexico">Music of Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WP10GDL10.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/WP10GDL10.JPG/220px-WP10GDL10.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/WP10GDL10.JPG/330px-WP10GDL10.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/WP10GDL10.JPG/440px-WP10GDL10.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3472" data-file-height="2604" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WP10GDL10.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">Mariachi</a> group playing at the 10th anniversary celebration of Wikipedia in <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a>. Mariachi is a musical expression inscribed in the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_List" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage List">UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage List</a> in 2011.</div></div></div>\n<p>Mexican society enjoys a vast array of music genres, showing the diversity of Mexican culture. Traditional music includes <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">mariachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banda_music" title="Banda music">banda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norte%C3%B1o_(music)" title="Norte\xc3\xb1o (music)">norte\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranchera" title="Ranchera">ranchera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corrido" title="Corrido">corridos</a>; on an everyday basis most Mexicans listen to contemporary music such as <a href="/wiki/Mexican_pop_music" title="Mexican pop music">pop</a>, rock, etc. in both English and Spanish. Mexico has the largest media industry in Latin America, producing Mexican artists who are famous in Central and South America and parts of Europe, especially Spain.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_cuisine" title="Mexican cuisine">Mexican cuisine</a></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_wine" title="Mexican wine">Mexican wine</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Drinking_chocolate,_Portland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Drinking_chocolate%2C_Portland.jpg/200px-Drinking_chocolate%2C_Portland.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Drinking_chocolate%2C_Portland.jpg/300px-Drinking_chocolate%2C_Portland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Drinking_chocolate%2C_Portland.jpg/400px-Drinking_chocolate%2C_Portland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The first <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a> version (liquid) was made by indigenous people in present-day Mexico, and was exported from Mexico to Europe after the Spanish conquest.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG/200px-Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG/300px-Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG/400px-Comida_en_la_Feria_del_Mole_2014_12.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i><a href="/wiki/Mole_sauce" title="Mole sauce">Mole sauce</a></i>, which has dozens of varieties across the Republic, is seen as a symbol of <i>Mexicanidad</i><sup id="cite_ref-Mole_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mole-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> and is considered Mexico\'s national dish.<sup id="cite_ref-Mole_347-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mole-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2005, Mexico presented the candidature of its gastronomy for <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> of UNESCO, being the first occasion in which a country had presented its gastronomic tradition for this purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> However, in a first instance the result was negative, because the committee did not place the proper emphasis on the importance of <a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">corn</a> in Mexican cuisine.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> Finally, on November 16 of 2010 Mexican gastronomy was recognized as <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">Intangible cultural heritage</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GastronomiaPatrimonio_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GastronomiaPatrimonio-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The origin of the current Mexican cuisine is established during the Spanish colonization, being a mixture of the foods of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and the native indigenous.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> Of foods originated in Mexico is the <a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">corn</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">pepper vegetables</a> (together with Central and South America), <a href="/wiki/Calabaza" title="Calabaza">calabazas</a> (together with the Americas), <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a> (together with Central and South America), the <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">turkey</a> (together with the Americas) and other fruits and spices. Other Indigenous products are many <a href="/wiki/Beans" class="mw-redirect" title="Beans">beans</a>. Similarly, some cooking techniques used today are inherited from pre-Hispanic peoples, such as the <a href="/wiki/Nixtamalization" title="Nixtamalization">nixtamalization</a> of corn, the cooking of food in ovens at ground level, grinding in <a href="/wiki/Molcajete" title="Molcajete">molcajete</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metate" title="Metate">metate</a>. With the Spaniards came the pork, beef and chicken meats; <a href="/wiki/Piper_(plant)" title="Piper (plant)">peppercorn</a>, sugar, milk and all its derivatives, wheat and rice, citrus fruits and another constellation of ingredients that are part of the daily diet of Mexicans.\n</p><p>From this meeting of millennia old two culinary traditions, were born <a href="/wiki/Pozole" title="Pozole">pozole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mole_sauce" title="Mole sauce">mole sauce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbacoa" title="Barbacoa">barbacoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamale" title="Tamale">tamale</a> is in its current forms, the <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a>, a large range of <a href="/wiki/Mexican_breads" title="Mexican breads">breads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taco" title="Taco">tacos</a>, and the broad repertoire of <a href="/wiki/Mexican_street_food" title="Mexican street food">Mexican street foods</a>. Beverages such as <a href="/wiki/Atole" title="Atole">atole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Champurrado" title="Champurrado">champurrado</a>, milk chocolate and <a href="/wiki/Aguas_frescas" title="Aguas frescas">aguas frescas</a> were born; desserts such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Acitr%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Acitr\xc3\xb3n (page does not exist)">acitr\xc3\xb3n</a> and the full range of crystallized sweets, <a href="/wiki/Rompope" title="Rompope">rompope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cajeta" title="Cajeta">cajeta</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jericaya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jericaya (page does not exist)">jericaya</a> and the wide repertoire of delights created in the convents of nuns in all parts of the country.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Mexico" title="Sport in Mexico">Sport in Mexico</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Azteca,_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg/220px-Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg/330px-Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg/440px-Estadio_Azteca%2C_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="618" data-file-height="355" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Azteca,_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Azteca" title="Estadio Azteca">Estadio Azteca</a>, regarded as one of the iconic football stadiums in the world, hosted the 1970 and 1986 World Cup finals and was the main venue of the 1968 Summer Olympics.</div></div></div>\n<p>Mexico\'s most popular sport is association football. It is commonly believed that football was introduced in Mexico by <a href="/wiki/Cornish_people" title="Cornish people">Cornish</a> miners at the end of the 19th century. By 1902 a five-team league had emerged with a strong British influence.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> Mexico\'s top clubs are <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club Am\xc3\xa9rica">Am\xc3\xa9rica</a> with 12 championships, <a
